<p><b>California</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a4/En-us-California.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-California.ogg" title="File:En-us-California.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɪ/ or /ə/ 'e' in 'roses'">ᵻ</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/ɔːr/ 'or' in 'abhor'">ɔːr</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/j/ 'y' in 'yes'">j</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>, <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/-/ affix">-</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/./ syllable break">.</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i><b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">KAL</span></span></b>-ə-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">FORN</span></span></b>-yə</i></a></span>, <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i><b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">KAL</span></span></b>-ə-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">FORN</span></span></b>-ee-ə</i></a></span>) is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">most populous state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of U.S. states by area">third most extensive</a> by area. Located on the western (<a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>) coast of the U.S., California is bordered by the other U.S. states of <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> and shares an <a href="/wiki/Mexico-United_States_border" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexico-United States border">international border</a> with the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Mexico" title="States of Mexico">Mexican state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a>. The state capital is <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento</a>. <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> is California's <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_California_cities_by_population" title="List of largest California cities by population">most populous city</a>, and the country's <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">second largest</a> after <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. The state also has the nation's <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_most_populous_counties_in_the_United_States" title="List of the most populous counties in the United States">most populous county</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County,_California" title="Los Angeles County, California">Los Angeles County</a>, and its <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_counties_in_the_United_States_by_area" title="List of the largest counties in the United States by area">largest county</a> by area, <a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino_County,_California" title="San Bernardino County, California">San Bernardino County</a>.</p>
<p>California's diverse geography ranges from the <a href="/wiki/Coastal_California" title="Coastal California">Pacific Coast</a> in the west to the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">Sierra Nevada</a> mountain range in the east; and from the <a href="/wiki/Sequoia_sempervirens" title="Sequoia sempervirens">redwood</a>–<a href="/wiki/Douglas_fir" title="Douglas fir">Douglas fir</a> forests in the northwest to the <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">Mojave Desert</a> in the southeast. The <a href="/wiki/California_Central_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="California Central Valley">Central Valley</a>, a major agricultural area, dominates the state's center. Though California is well-known for its warm <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a>, the large size of the state means it can vary from moist <a href="/wiki/Temperate_rainforest" title="Temperate rainforest">temperate rainforest</a> in the north, to arid <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desert</a> in the interior, as well as snowy <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine</a> in the mountains.</p>
<p>What is now California was first settled by <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_California" title="Indigenous peoples of California">various Native American tribes</a> before being explored by a number of European expeditions during the 16th and 17th centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> then claimed it as part of <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> in their <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a> colony. The area became a part of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> in 1821 following its successful <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">war for independence</a>, but was ceded to the United States in 1848 after the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a>. The western portion of Alta California then was organized as the State of California, and admitted as the 31st state on September 9, 1850. The <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">California Gold Rush</a> starting in 1848 led to dramatic social and demographic changes, with large-scale emigration from the east and abroad with an accompanying economic boom.</p>
<p>If it were a country, California would be the <a href="/wiki/Comparison_between_U.S._states_and_countries_nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Comparison between U.S. states and countries nominal GDP">6th largest economy in the world</a><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population">35th most populous</a>. It is also regarded as a global trendsetter in both popular culture and politics, and is the origin of the <a href="/wiki/Film_industry" title="Film industry">film industry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hippie" title="Hippie">hippie</a> counterculture, the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computer</a>, among others. Fifty-eight percent of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_California" title="Economy of California">state's economy</a> is centered on <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forms_of_government" title="Forms of government">government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a>, and professional, scientific and technical <a href="/wiki/Business_services" class="mw-redirect" title="Business services">business services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BEA_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BEA-16">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a> has the nation's <a href="/wiki/Highest-income_metropolitan_statistical_areas_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Highest-income metropolitan statistical areas in the United States">highest median household income</a> by metropolitan area, and is the headquarters of three of the world's largest 20 firms by revenue, <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, and <a href="/wiki/McKesson_Corporation" title="McKesson Corporation">McKesson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Although it accounts for only 1.5 percent of the state's economy,<sup id="cite_ref-BEA_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BEA-16">[16]</a></sup> California's agriculture industry has the highest output of any U.S. state.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Etymology_of_California" title="Etymology of California">Etymology of California</a></div>
<p>The word <i>California</i> originally referred to the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> of Mexico; it was later extended to the entire region composed of the current United States states of California, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, and parts of <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The name <i>California</i> is surmised by some writers to have derived from a fictional paradise peopled by <a href="/wiki/Black_People" class="mw-redirect" title="Black People">Black</a> <a href="/wiki/Amazons" title="Amazons">Amazons</a> and ruled by Queen <a href="/wiki/Calafia" title="Calafia">Calafia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> who fought alongside Muslims and whose name was chosen to echo the title of a Muslim leader, the Caliph, fictionally implying that California was the Caliphate.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The story of Calafia is recorded in a 1510 work <i><a href="/wiki/Las_sergas_de_Esplandi%C3%A1n" title="Las sergas de Esplandián">The Adventures of Esplandián</a></i>, written as a sequel to <i><a href="/wiki/Amadis_de_Gaula" class="mw-redirect" title="Amadis de Gaula">Amadis de Gaula</a></i> by Spanish adventure writer <a href="/wiki/Garci_Rodr%C3%ADguez_de_Montalvo" title="Garci Rodríguez de Montalvo">Garci Rodríguez de Montalvo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cpn_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpn-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lavender_1987_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lavender_1987-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The kingdom of Queen Calafia, according to Montalvo, was said to be a remote land inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Griffin" title="Griffin">griffins</a> and other strange beasts, and rich in gold.</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Know ye that at the right hand of the Indies there is an island called California, very close to that part of the Terrestrial Paradise, which was inhabited by black women without a single man among them, and they lived in the manner of Amazons. They were robust of body with strong passionate hearts and great virtue. The island itself is one of the wildest in the world on account of the bold and craggy rocks.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— Chapter CLVII of <i><a href="/wiki/Las_sergas_de_Esplandi%C3%A1n" title="Las sergas de Esplandián">The Adventures of Esplandián</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>When Spanish explorer <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Ulloa" title="Francisco de Ulloa">Francisco de Ulloa</a> was exploring the western coast of North America, his initial surveys of the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> led him to believe that it was an island rather than part of the larger continent, so he dubbed the "island" after the mythical island in Montalvo's writing.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> This conventional wisdom that <a href="/wiki/Island_of_California" title="Island of California">California was an island</a>, with maps drawn to reflect this belief, lasted as late as the 1700s.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortened forms of the state's name include <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_abbreviations" title="List of U.S. state abbreviations">CA, Cal., Calif.</a> and <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166" title="ISO 3166">US-CA</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_California" title="History of California">History of California</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-contact">Pre-contact</span></h3>
<p>Settled by successive waves of arrivals during the last 10,000 years, California was one of the most culturally and linguistically diverse areas in <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_North_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-Columbian North America">pre-Columbian North America</a>. Various estimates of the native population range from 100,000 to 300,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStarr200713_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStarr200713-28">[28]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_California" title="Indigenous peoples of California">Indigenous peoples of California</a> included more than <a href="/wiki/Classification_of_indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas#California" title="Classification of indigenous peoples of the Americas">70 distinct groups</a> of Native Americans, ranging from large, settled populations living on the coast to groups in the interior. California groups also were diverse in their political organization with bands, tribes, villages, and on the resource-rich coasts, large chiefdoms, such as the <a href="/wiki/Chumash_people" title="Chumash people">Chumash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pomo_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pomo people">Pomo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salinan" title="Salinan">Salinan</a>. Trade, intermarriage and military alliances fostered many social and economic relationships among the diverse groups.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th.2C_17th_and_18th_centuries">16th, 17th and 18th centuries</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcala_in_1848.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcala_in_1848.jpg/220px-Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcala_in_1848.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcala_in_1848.jpg/330px-Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcala_in_1848.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcala_in_1848.jpg/440px-Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcala_in_1848.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1029" data-file-height="593" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcala_in_1848.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcal%C3%A1" title="Mission San Diego de Alcalá">Mission San Diego de Alcalá</a> drawn as it was in 1848. Established in 1769, it was the first of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_missions_in_California" title="Spanish missions in California">California Missions.</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first European effort to explore the coast as far north as the <a href="/wiki/Russian_River_(California)" title="Russian River (California)">Russian River</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish</a> sailing expedition, led by Portuguese captain <a href="/wiki/Juan_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Cabrillo" title="Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo">Juan Rodríguez Cabrillo</a>, in 1542. Some 37 years later English explorer <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">Francis Drake</a> also explored and claimed an undefined portion of the California coast in 1579. Spanish traders made unintended visits with the <a href="/wiki/Manila_galleon" title="Manila galleon">Manila galleons</a> on their return trips from the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> beginning in 1565.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The first Asians to set foot on what would be the United States occurred in 1587, when <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Filipino" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Filipino">Filipino</a> sailors arrived in Spanish ships at <a href="/wiki/Morro_Bay,_California" title="Morro Bay, California">Morro Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A1n_Vizca%C3%ADno" title="Sebastián Vizcaíno">Sebastián Vizcaíno</a> explored and mapped the coast of California in 1602 for <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>.</p>
<p>Despite the on-the-ground explorations of California in the 16th century, Rodríguez's idea of California as an island persisted. That depiction appeared on many European maps well into the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Portol%C3%A0_expedition" class="mw-redirect" title="Portolà expedition">Portolà expedition</a> of 1769–70, Spanish <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a> began setting up 21 <a href="/wiki/Spanish_missions_in_California" title="Spanish missions in California">California Missions</a> on or near the coast of <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta (Upper) California</a>, beginning in San Diego. During the same period, Spanish military forces built several forts (<i><a href="/wiki/Presidio" title="Presidio">presidios</a></i>) and three small towns (<i>pueblos</i>). Two of the pueblos grew into the cities of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose</a>. The Spanish colonization brought the <a href="/wiki/California_Genocide" title="California Genocide">genocide of the indigenous Californian peoples</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Vue_de_l%E2%80%99etablissement_russe_de_la_Bodega,_%C3%A0_la_C%C3%B4te_de_la_Nouvelle_Albion,_en_1828.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Vue_de_l%E2%80%99etablissement_russe_de_la_Bodega%2C_%C3%A0_la_C%C3%B4te_de_la_Nouvelle_Albion%2C_en_1828.jpg/220px-Vue_de_l%E2%80%99etablissement_russe_de_la_Bodega%2C_%C3%A0_la_C%C3%B4te_de_la_Nouvelle_Albion%2C_en_1828.jpg" width="220" height="152" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Vue_de_l%E2%80%99etablissement_russe_de_la_Bodega%2C_%C3%A0_la_C%C3%B4te_de_la_Nouvelle_Albion%2C_en_1828.jpg/330px-Vue_de_l%E2%80%99etablissement_russe_de_la_Bodega%2C_%C3%A0_la_C%C3%B4te_de_la_Nouvelle_Albion%2C_en_1828.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Vue_de_l%E2%80%99etablissement_russe_de_la_Bodega%2C_%C3%A0_la_C%C3%B4te_de_la_Nouvelle_Albion%2C_en_1828.jpg/440px-Vue_de_l%E2%80%99etablissement_russe_de_la_Bodega%2C_%C3%A0_la_C%C3%B4te_de_la_Nouvelle_Albion%2C_en_1828.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3893" data-file-height="2684" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">The Russian Empire</a> established their largest settlement in California at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ross,_California" title="Fort Ross, California">Fort Ross</a> in 1812</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:California1838.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/California1838.jpg/220px-California1838.jpg" width="220" height="308" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/California1838.jpg/330px-California1838.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/California1838.jpg/440px-California1838.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2243" data-file-height="3139" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Map showing <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> in 1838 when it was a sparsely populated Mexican province.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg/220px-SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg" width="220" height="148" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg/330px-SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg/440px-SanFranciscoharbor1851c_sharp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2574" data-file-height="1727" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Merchant ships fill <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> harbor in 1850 or 1851</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Chinese_Gold_Miners_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chinese_Gold_Miners_b.jpg/220px-Chinese_Gold_Miners_b.jpg" width="220" height="171" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chinese_Gold_Miners_b.jpg/330px-Chinese_Gold_Miners_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chinese_Gold_Miners_b.jpg/440px-Chinese_Gold_Miners_b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="531" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Chinese_American_history#California_Gold_Rush" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese American history">Chinese gold miners</a> in California</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Imperial Russia</a> explored the California coast and established a trading post at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ross" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Ross">Fort Ross</a>. Its early 19th-century coastal settlements north of <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">San Francisco Bay</a> constituted the southernmost Russian colony in North America and were spread over an area stretching from <a href="/wiki/Point_Arena,_California" title="Point Arena, California">Point Arena</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tomales_Bay" title="Tomales Bay">Tomales Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Historical_Atlas_of_California_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historical_Atlas_of_California-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1821, the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexican War of Independence</a> gave <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (including California) independence from Spain; for the next 25 years, <a href="/wiki/Alta_California" title="Alta California">Alta California</a> remained a remote northern province of the nation of Mexico.</p>
<p>Cattle ranches, or <i><a href="/wiki/Ranchos_of_California" title="Ranchos of California">ranchos</a></i>, emerged as the dominant institutions of Mexican California. After Mexican independence from Spain, the chain of missions became the property of the Mexican government and were <a href="/wiki/Secularized" class="mw-redirect" title="Secularized">secularized</a> by 1834.<sup id="cite_ref-nps_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nps-34">[34]</a></sup> The ranchos developed under ownership by <a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">Californios</a> (Spanish-speaking Californians) who had received land grants, and traded cowhides and tallow with Boston merchants.</p>
<p>From the 1820s, trappers and settlers from the United States and the future Canada arrived in Northern California. These new arrivals used the <a href="/wiki/Siskiyou_Trail" title="Siskiyou Trail">Siskiyou Trail</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_Trail" title="California Trail">California Trail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Trail" title="Oregon Trail">Oregon Trail</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Spanish_Trail_(trade_route)" title="Old Spanish Trail (trade route)">Old Spanish Trail</a> to cross the rugged mountains and harsh deserts in and surrounding California.</p>
<p>Between 1831 and 1836, California experienced a series of revolts against Mexico;<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> this culminated in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=1836_California_revolt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1836 California revolt (page does not exist)">1836 California revolt</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bautista_Alvarado" title="Juan Bautista Alvarado">Juan Bautista Alvarado</a>, which ended after Mexico appointed him governor of the department.<sup id="cite_ref-Starr2007_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Starr2007-36">[36]</a></sup> The revolt, which had momentarily declared California an independent state, was successful with the assistance of <a href="/wiki/Americans" title="Americans">American</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">British</a> residents of California,<sup id="cite_ref-Graham1840_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Graham1840-37">[37]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Graham" title="Isaac Graham">Isaac Graham</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> after 1840, 100 of those residents who did not have passports were arrested, leading to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Graham_affair&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Graham affair (page does not exist)">Graham affair</a> in 1840.<sup id="cite_ref-Graham1840_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Graham1840-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>One of the largest ranchers in California was <a href="/wiki/John_Marsh_(pioneer)" title="John Marsh (pioneer)">John Marsh</a>. After failing to obtain justice against squatters on his land from the Mexican courts, he determined that California should become part of the United States. Marsh conducted a letter-writing campaign espousing the California climate, soil and other reasons to settle there, as well as the best route to follow, which became known as "Marsh's route." His letters were read, reread, passed around, and printed in newspapers throughout the country, and started the first wagon trains rolling to California.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> He invited immigrants to stay on his ranch until they could get settled, and assisted in their obtaining passports.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>After ushering in the period of organized emigration to California, Marsh helped end the rule of the last Mexican governor of California, thereby paving the way to California's ultimate acquisition by the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1846, settlers rebelled against Mexican rule during the <a href="/wiki/Bear_Flag_Revolt#Bear_Flag_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Bear Flag Revolt">Bear Flag Revolt</a>. Afterwards, rebels raised the <a href="/wiki/Bear_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Bear Flag">Bear Flag</a> (featuring a bear, a star, a red stripe and the words "California Republic") at Sonoma. The Republic's only president was <a href="/wiki/William_B._Ide" title="William B. Ide">William B. Ide</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-William_B._Ide_Adobe_SHP_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-William_B._Ide_Adobe_SHP-42">[42]</a></sup> who played a pivotal role during the Bear Flag Revolt.</p>
<p>The California Republic was short lived;<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> the same year marked the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a> (1846–48).<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> When Commodore <a href="/wiki/John_D._Sloat" title="John D. Sloat">John D. Sloat</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> sailed into <a href="/wiki/Monterey_Bay" title="Monterey Bay">Monterey Bay</a> and began the military occupation of California by the United States, Northern California capitulated in less than a month to the United States forces.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> After a series of defensive battles in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Cahuenga" title="Treaty of Cahuenga">Treaty of Cahuenga</a> was signed by the <a href="/wiki/Californios" class="mw-redirect" title="Californios">Californios</a> on January 13, 1847, securing American control in California.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</a> that ended the war, the western territory of Alta California, became the United States state of California, and <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> became United States Territories. The lightly populated lower region of California, the Baja Peninsula, remained in the possession of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.</p>
<p>In 1846, the non-native population of California was estimated to be no more than 8,000, plus about 100,000 Native Americans down from about 300,000 before Hispanic settlement in 1769.<sup id="cite_ref-Osborne2012_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Osborne2012-47">[47]</a></sup> After gold was discovered in 1848, the population burgeoned with United States citizens, Europeans, Chinese and other immigrants during the great <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">California Gold Rush</a>. By 1854 over 300,000 settlers had come.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Between 1847 and 1870, the population of <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> increased from 500 to 150,000.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> On September 9, 1850, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1850" title="Compromise of 1850">Compromise of 1850</a>, California was admitted to the United States undivided as a <a href="/wiki/Free_state_(USA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Free state (USA)">free state</a>, denying the expansion of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">slavery</a> to the Pacific Coast.</p>
<p>California's native population precipitously declined, above all, from Eurasian diseases to which they had no natural immunity.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> As in other states, the native inhabitants were forcibly removed from their lands by incoming miners, ranchers, and farmers. And although California entered the union as a free state, the "loitering or orphaned Indians" were de facto enslaved by Mexican and Anglo-American masters under the 1853 <i>Act for the Government and Protection of Indians</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cabrillo1_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cabrillo1-51">[51]</a></sup> There were massacres in which hundreds of indigenous people were killed. Between 1850 and 1860, California paid around 1.5 million dollars (some 250,000 of which was reimbursed by the federal government)<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> to hire militias whose purpose was to protect settlers from the indigenous populations. In later decades, the native population was placed in reservations and rancherias, which were often small and isolated and without enough natural resources or funding from the government to sustain the populations living on them.<sup id="cite_ref-cabrillo1_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cabrillo1-51">[51]</a></sup> As a result, the rise of California was a calamity for the native inhabitants. Several scholars and Native American activists, including Benjamin Madley and <a href="/wiki/Ed_Castillo" title="Ed Castillo">Ed Castillo</a>, have described the actions of the California government as a genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>The seat of government for California under Spanish and later Mexican rule was located at <a href="/wiki/Monterey,_California" title="Monterey, California">Monterey</a> from 1777 until 1845.<sup id="cite_ref-nps_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nps-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pio_Pico" class="mw-redirect" title="Pio Pico">Pio Pico</a>, last Mexican governor of Alta California, moved the capital to Los Angeles in 1845. The United States <a href="/wiki/Consulate" class="mw-redirect" title="Consulate">consulate</a> was also located in Monterey, under consul <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Larkin" title="Thomas O. Larkin">Thomas O. Larkin</a>.</p>
<p>In 1849, the Constitutional Convention was first held in Monterey. Among the tasks was a decision on a location for the new state capital. The first legislative sessions were held in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose</a> (1850–1851). Subsequent locations included <a href="/wiki/Vallejo,_California" title="Vallejo, California">Vallejo</a> (1852–1853), and nearby <a href="/wiki/Benicia,_California" title="Benicia, California">Benicia</a> (1853–1854); these locations eventually proved to be inadequate as well. The capital has been located in <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento</a> since 1854<sup id="cite_ref-Wilson_2006_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson_2006-54">[54]</a></sup> with only a short break in 1862 when legislative sessions were held in San Francisco due to <a href="/wiki/Great_Flood_of_1862" title="Great Flood of 1862">flooding in Sacramento</a>.</p>
<p>Initially, travel between California and the rest of the continental United States was time consuming and dangerous. A more direct connection came in 1869 with the completion of the <a href="/wiki/First_Transcontinental_Railroad" title="First Transcontinental Railroad">First Transcontinental Railroad</a> through <a href="/wiki/Donner_Pass" title="Donner Pass">Donner Pass</a> in the Sierra Nevada mountains. Once completed, hundreds of thousands of United States citizens came west, where new Californians were discovering that land in the state, if irrigated during the dry summer months, was extremely well suited to fruit cultivation and agriculture in general. Vast expanses of wheat, other cereal crops, vegetable crops, cotton, and nut and fruit trees were grown (including oranges in Southern California), and the foundation was laid for the state's prodigious agricultural production in the Central Valley and elsewhere.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hollywood-Studios-1922.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Hollywood-Studios-1922.jpg/220px-Hollywood-Studios-1922.jpg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Hollywood-Studios-1922.jpg/330px-Hollywood-Studios-1922.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Hollywood-Studios-1922.jpg/440px-Hollywood-Studios-1922.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="621" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hollywood-Studios-1922.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hollywood film studios, 1922</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Migration to California accelerated during the early 20th century with the completion of major transcontinental highways like the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Highway" title="Lincoln Highway">Lincoln Highway</a> and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_66_(California)" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Route 66 (California)">Route 66</a>. In the period from 1900 to 1965, the population grew from fewer than one million to become the most populous state in the Union. In 1940, the Census Bureau reported California's population as 6.0% Hispanic, 2.4% Asian, and 89.5% non-Hispanic white.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>To meet the population's needs, major engineering feats like the <a href="/wiki/California_Aqueduct" title="California Aqueduct">California</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Aqueduct" title="Los Angeles Aqueduct">Los Angeles Aqueducts</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Oroville_Dam" title="Oroville Dam">Oroville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shasta_Dam" title="Shasta Dam">Shasta Dams</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco%E2%80%93Oakland_Bay_Bridge" title="San Francisco–Oakland Bay Bridge">Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Bridge" title="Golden Gate Bridge">Golden Gate</a> Bridges were built across the state. The state government also adopted the <a href="/wiki/California_Master_Plan_for_Higher_Education" title="California Master Plan for Higher Education">California Master Plan for Higher Education</a> in 1960 to develop a highly efficient system of public education.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, attracted to the mild Mediterranean climate, cheap land, and the state's wide variety of geography, filmmakers established the <a href="/wiki/Studio_system" title="Studio system">studio system</a> in Hollywood in the 1920s. California manufactured 8.7 percent of total United States military armaments produced during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, ranking third (behind <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="New York (state)">New York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>) among the 48 states.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> After World War II, California's economy greatly expanded due to strong <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_manufacturer" title="Aerospace manufacturer">aerospace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Defense_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Defense industry">defense</a> industries,<sup id="cite_ref-BWatkins2012_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWatkins2012-57">[57]</a></sup> whose size decreased following the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BWatkins2012_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BWatkins2012-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> and its Dean of Engineering <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Terman" title="Frederick Terman">Frederick Terman</a> began encouraging faculty and graduates to stay in California instead of leaving the state, and develop a high-tech region in the area now known as <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Markoff_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Markoff-59">[59]</a></sup> As a result of these efforts, California is regarded as a world center of the entertainment and music industries, of technology, engineering, and the aerospace industry, and as the United States center of agricultural production.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen2003115.E2.80.93116_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen2003115.E2.80.93116-60">[60]</a></sup> Just before the <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">"Dot Com Bust"</a> California had the 5th largest economy in the world among nations.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Yet since 1991, and starting in the late 1980s in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>, California has seen a net loss of domestic migrants most years. This is often referred to by the media as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=California_exodus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="California exodus (page does not exist)">California exodus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, during the 20th century, two great disasters happened in California. The <a href="/wiki/1906_San_Francisco_earthquake" title="1906 San Francisco earthquake">1906 San Francisco earthquake</a> and 1928 <a href="/wiki/St._Francis_Dam" title="St. Francis Dam">St. Francis Dam</a> flood remain the deadliest in U.S history.<sup id="cite_ref-IIIMcNeill2004_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IIIMcNeill2004-63">[63]</a></sup></p>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>California is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of U.S. states by area">3rd largest state in the United States</a> in area, after <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> and <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2000_population_and_housing_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2000_population_and_housing-65">[65]</a></sup> California is often geographically bisected into two regions, <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>, comprising the 10 southernmost counties,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">Northern California</a>, comprising the 48 northernmost counties.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the middle of the state lies the <a href="/wiki/California_Central_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="California Central Valley">California Central Valley</a>, bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">Sierra Nevada</a> in the east, the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Coast_Ranges" title="Pacific Coast Ranges">coastal mountain ranges</a> in the west, the <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Range" title="Cascade Range">Cascade Range</a> to the north and by the <a href="/wiki/Tehachapi_Mountains" title="Tehachapi Mountains">Tehachapi Mountains</a> in the south. The Central Valley is California's productive agricultural heartland.</p>
<p>Divided in two by the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento-San_Joaquin_River_Delta" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacramento-San Joaquin River Delta">Sacramento-San Joaquin River Delta</a>, the northern portion, the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_Valley" title="Sacramento Valley">Sacramento Valley</a> serves as the watershed of the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_River" title="Sacramento River">Sacramento River</a>, while the southern portion, the <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley" title="San Joaquin Valley">San Joaquin Valley</a> is the watershed for the <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_River" title="San Joaquin River">San Joaquin River</a>. Both valleys derive their names from the rivers that flow through them. With dredging, the Sacramento and the San Joaquin Rivers have remained deep enough for several inland cities to be <a href="/wiki/Seaport" class="mw-redirect" title="Seaport">seaports</a>.</p>
<p>The Sacramento-San Joaquin River Delta is a critical water supply hub for the state. Water is diverted from the delta and through an extensive network of <a href="/wiki/Pump_(Water)" title="Pump (Water)">pumps</a> and canals that traverse nearly the length of the state, to the Central Valley and the State Water Projects and other needs. Water from the Delta provides drinking water for nearly 23 million people, almost two-thirds of the state's population as well as water for farmers on the west side of the San Joaquin Valley.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands_of_California" title="Channel Islands of California">Channel Islands</a> are located off the <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern</a> <a href="/wiki/South_Coast_(California)" title="South Coast (California)">coast</a>.</p>
<p>The Sierra Nevada (Spanish for "snowy range") includes the highest peak in the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous 48 states</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Whitney" title="Mount Whitney">Mount Whitney</a>, at 14,505 feet (4,421&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-Mount_Whitney_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mount_Whitney-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NAVD88_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAVD88-8">[8]</a></sup> The range embraces <a href="/wiki/Yosemite_Valley" title="Yosemite Valley">Yosemite Valley</a>, famous for its glacially carved domes, and <a href="/wiki/Sequoia_National_Park" title="Sequoia National Park">Sequoia National Park</a>, home to the <a href="/wiki/Sequoiadendron_giganteum" title="Sequoiadendron giganteum">giant sequoia</a> trees, the largest living organisms on Earth, and the deep freshwater lake, <a href="/wiki/Lake_Tahoe" title="Lake Tahoe">Lake Tahoe</a>, the largest lake in the state by volume.</p>
<p>To the east of the Sierra Nevada are <a href="/wiki/Owens_Valley" title="Owens Valley">Owens Valley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mono_Lake" title="Mono Lake">Mono Lake</a>, an essential <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">migratory bird</a> habitat. In the western part of the state is <a href="/wiki/Clear_Lake_(California)" title="Clear Lake (California)">Clear Lake</a>, the largest freshwater lake by area entirely in California. Though Lake Tahoe is larger, it is divided by the California/Nevada border. The Sierra Nevada falls to Arctic temperatures in winter and has several dozen small glaciers, including <a href="/wiki/Palisade_Glacier" title="Palisade Glacier">Palisade Glacier</a>, the southernmost glacier in the United States.</p>
<p>About 45 percent of the state's total surface area is covered by forests,<sup id="cite_ref-Forestry_2003_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forestry_2003-70">[70]</a></sup> and California's diversity of pine species is unmatched by any other state. California contains more forestland than any other state except Alaska. Many of the trees in the <a href="/wiki/White_Mountains_(California)" title="White Mountains (California)">California White Mountains</a> are the oldest in the world; an individual <a href="/wiki/Bristlecone_pine" title="Bristlecone pine">bristlecone pine</a> is over 5,000 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-Lanner_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lanner-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oldest_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oldest-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the south is a large inland salt lake, the <a href="/wiki/Salton_Sea" title="Salton Sea">Salton Sea</a>. The south-central desert is called the <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">Mojave</a>; to the northeast of the Mojave lies <a href="/wiki/Death_Valley" title="Death Valley">Death Valley</a>, which contains the lowest and hottest place in North America, the <a href="/wiki/Badwater_Basin" title="Badwater Basin">Badwater Basin</a> at −279 feet (−85&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-NED_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NED-10">[10]</a></sup> The horizontal distance from the bottom of Death Valley to the top of Mount Whitney is less than 90 miles (140&#160;km). Indeed, almost all of southeastern California is arid, hot desert, with routine extreme high temperatures during the summer. The southeastern border of California with Arizona is entirely formed by the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a>, from which the southern part of the state gets about half of its water.</p>
<p>California contains both the highest point (<a href="/wiki/Mount_Whitney" title="Mount Whitney">Mount Whitney</a>) and the lowest point (<a href="/wiki/Death_Valley" title="Death Valley">Death Valley</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">contiguous United States</a>.</p>
<p>A majority of California's cities are located in either the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_metropolitan_area" title="Sacramento metropolitan area">Sacramento metropolitan area</a> in <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">Northern California</a>; or the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area" title="Los Angeles metropolitan area">Los Angeles area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Inland_Empire" title="Inland Empire">Riverside-San Bernardino-Inland Empire</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego metropolitan area">San Diego metropolitan area</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>. The Los Angeles Area, the Bay Area, and the San Diego metropolitan area are among several major metropolitan areas along the California coast.</p>
<p>As part of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ring_of_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Ring of Fire">Ring of Fire</a>, California is subject to <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunamis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">floods</a>, droughts, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_winds" title="Santa Ana winds">Santa Ana winds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">wildfires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Landslide" title="Landslide">landslides</a> on steep terrain, and has several <a href="/wiki/Volcanoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanoes">volcanoes</a>. It has many <a href="/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_California" title="List of earthquakes in California">earthquakes</a> due to several faults running through the state, in particular the <a href="/wiki/San_Andreas_Fault" title="San Andreas Fault">San Andreas Fault</a>. About 37,000 <a href="/wiki/Earthquake" title="Earthquake">earthquakes</a> are recorded each year, but most are too small to be felt.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_California" title="Climate of California">Climate of California</a></div>
<p>Although most of the state has a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a>, due to the state's large size, the climate ranges from <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical</a>. The cool <a href="/wiki/California_Current" title="California Current">California Current</a> offshore often creates summer <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">fog</a> near the coast. Farther inland, there are colder winters and hotter summers. The maritime moderation results in the shoreline summertime temperatures of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> being the coolest of all major metropolitan areas of the United States and uniquely cool compared to areas on the same latitude in the interior and on the east coast of the North American continent. Even the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a> shoreline bordering Mexico is cooler in summer than most areas in the contiguous United States. Just a few miles inland, summer temperature extremes are significantly higher, with downtown Los Angeles being several degrees <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_Los_Angeles_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of the Los Angeles Basin">warmer</a> than at the coast. The same <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimate</a> phenomenon is seen in the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area#Climate" title="San Francisco Bay Area">climate</a> of the Bay Area, where areas sheltered from the sea experience significantly hotter summers than nearby areas that are close to the ocean.</p>
<p>Northern parts of the state have more rain than the south. California's mountain ranges also influence the climate: some of the rainiest parts of the state are west-facing mountain slopes. Northwestern California has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate climate</a>, and the Central Valley has a Mediterranean climate but with greater temperature extremes than the coast. The high mountains, including the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">Sierra Nevada</a>, have an <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine climate</a> with snow in winter and mild to moderate heat in summer.</p>
<p>California's mountains produce <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">rain shadows</a> on the eastern side, creating extensive <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">deserts</a>. The higher elevation deserts of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_California" title="Eastern California">eastern California</a> have hot summers and cold winters, while the low deserts east of the Southern California mountains have hot summers and nearly frostless mild winters. <a href="/wiki/Death_Valley" title="Death Valley">Death Valley</a>, a desert with large expanses below sea level, is considered the hottest location in the world; the highest temperature in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-newRecord_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newRecord-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> 134&#160;°F (56.7&#160;°C), was recorded there on July 10, 1913. The lowest temperature in California was −45&#160;°F (−43&#160;°C) in 1937 in <a href="/wiki/Boca,_California" title="Boca, California">Boca</a>.</p>
<p>The table below lists average temperatures for August and December in a selection of places throughout the state; some highly populated and some not. This includes the relatively cool summers of the <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Bay" title="Humboldt Bay">Humboldt Bay</a> region around <a href="/wiki/Eureka,_California" title="Eureka, California">Eureka</a>, the extreme heat of <a href="/wiki/Death_Valley" title="Death Valley">Death Valley</a>, and the mountain climate of <a href="/wiki/Mammoth_Lakes,_California" title="Mammoth Lakes, California">Mammoth</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(U.S.)" title="Sierra Nevada (U.S.)">Sierra Nevadas</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ecology_of_California" title="Ecology of California">Ecology of California</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_California" title="Environment of California">Environment of California</a></div>
<p>California is one of the richest and most diverse parts of the world, and includes some of the most endangered ecological communities. California is part of the <a href="/wiki/Nearctic_ecozone" class="mw-redirect" title="Nearctic ecozone">Nearctic ecozone</a> and spans a number of terrestrial <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Checklist_of_the_Scarabaeoidea_of_the_Nearctic_Realm_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Checklist_of_the_Scarabaeoidea_of_the_Nearctic_Realm-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>California's large number of <a href="/wiki/Endemic_(ecology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic (ecology)">endemic</a> species includes <a href="/wiki/Relict_(biology)" title="Relict (biology)">relict</a> species, which have died out elsewhere, such as the Catalina ironwood (<i><a href="/wiki/Lyonothamnus_floribundus" class="mw-redirect" title="Lyonothamnus floribundus">Lyonothamnus floribundus</a></i>). Many other endemics originated through differentiation or <a href="/wiki/Adaptive_radiation" title="Adaptive radiation">adaptive radiation</a>, whereby multiple species develop from a common ancestor to take advantage of diverse ecological conditions such as the California lilac (<i><a href="/wiki/Ceanothus" title="Ceanothus">Ceanothus</a></i>). Many California endemics have become endangered, as urbanization, logging, <a href="/wiki/Overgrazing" title="Overgrazing">overgrazing</a>, and the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Exotic_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Exotic species">exotic species</a> have encroached on their habitat.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_California" title="Fauna of California">Fauna of California</a> and <a href="/wiki/California_Floristic_Province" title="California Floristic Province">California Floristic Province</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_California_native_plants" title="List of California native plants">List of California native plants</a></div>
<p>California boasts several superlatives in its collection of flora: the <a href="/wiki/Giant_sequoia" class="mw-redirect" title="Giant sequoia">largest trees</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Coast_redwood" class="mw-redirect" title="Coast redwood">tallest trees</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pinus_longaeva" title="Pinus longaeva">oldest trees</a>. California's native grasses are <a href="/wiki/Perennial_plant" title="Perennial plant">perennial plants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Restoring_Native_Grasses_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Restoring_Native_Grasses-78">[78]</a></sup> After European contact, these were generally replaced by <a href="/wiki/Invasive_species" title="Invasive species">invasive species</a> of European annual grasses; and, in modern times, California's hills turn a characteristic golden-brown in summer.<sup id="cite_ref-The_California_Invasive_Species_List_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_California_Invasive_Species_List-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because California has the greatest diversity of climate and terrain, the state has six life zones which are the lower Sonoran (desert); upper Sonoran (foothill regions and some coastal lands), transition (coastal areas and moist northeastern counties); and the Canadian, Hudsonian, and Arctic Zones, comprising the state's highest elevations.<sup id="cite_ref-California:_flora_and_fauna_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Plant life in the dry climate of the lower Sonoran zone contains a diversity of native cactus, mesquite, and paloverde. The <a href="/wiki/Yucca_brevifolia" title="Yucca brevifolia">Joshua tree</a> is found in the Mojave Desert. Flowering plants include the dwarf desert poppy and a variety of <a href="/wiki/Aster_(genus)" title="Aster (genus)">asters</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fremont_cottonwood" class="mw-redirect" title="Fremont cottonwood">Fremont cottonwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valley_oak" class="mw-redirect" title="Valley oak">valley oak</a> thrive in the Central Valley. The upper Sonoran zone includes the chaparral belt, characterized by forests of small shrubs, stunted trees, and herbaceous plants. <i><a href="/wiki/Nemophila" title="Nemophila">Nemophila</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Lamiaceae" title="Lamiaceae">mint</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Phacelia" title="Phacelia">Phacelia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Viola_(plant)" title="Viola (plant)">Viola</a></i>, and the California poppy (<i><a href="/wiki/Eschscholzia_californica" title="Eschscholzia californica">Eschscholzia californica</a></i>) – the state flower – also flourish in this zone, along with the lupine, more species of which occur here than anywhere else in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-California:_flora_and_fauna_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The transition zone includes most of California's forests with the redwood (<i><a href="/wiki/Sequoia_sempervirens" title="Sequoia sempervirens">Sequoia sempervirens</a></i>) and the "big tree" or giant sequoia (<i><a href="/wiki/Sequoiadendron_giganteum" title="Sequoiadendron giganteum">Sequoiadendron giganteum</a></i>), among the oldest living things on earth (some are said to have lived at least 4,000 years). <a href="/wiki/Tanbark_oak" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanbark oak">Tanbark oak</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_laurel" class="mw-redirect" title="California laurel">California laurel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_pine" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugar pine">sugar pine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arbutus" title="Arbutus">madrona</a>, broad-leaved maple, and <a href="/wiki/Douglas-fir" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas-fir">Douglas-fir</a> also grow here. Forest floors are covered with <a href="/wiki/Polystichum" title="Polystichum">swordfern</a>, alumnroot, <a href="/wiki/Barrenwort" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrenwort">barrenwort</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trillium" title="Trillium">trillium</a>, and there are thickets of <a href="/wiki/Huckleberry" title="Huckleberry">huckleberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azalea" title="Azalea">azalea</a>, elder, and wild currant. Characteristic wild flowers include varieties of mariposa, <a href="/wiki/Tulip" title="Tulip">tulip</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lilium_columbianum" title="Lilium columbianum">tiger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lilium_pardalinum" title="Lilium pardalinum">leopard</a> lilies.<sup id="cite_ref-Sequoia_sempervirens_.28D._Don.29_Endl._81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sequoia_sempervirens_.28D._Don.29_Endl.-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Joshua_Tree_National_Park_(California,_USA)_--_2012_--_18.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Joshua_Tree_National_Park_%28California%2C_USA%29_--_2012_--_18.jpg/220px-Joshua_Tree_National_Park_%28California%2C_USA%29_--_2012_--_18.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Joshua_Tree_National_Park_%28California%2C_USA%29_--_2012_--_18.jpg/330px-Joshua_Tree_National_Park_%28California%2C_USA%29_--_2012_--_18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Joshua_Tree_National_Park_%28California%2C_USA%29_--_2012_--_18.jpg/440px-Joshua_Tree_National_Park_%28California%2C_USA%29_--_2012_--_18.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3800" data-file-height="2533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
