<i><a href="/wiki/Cylindropuntia_bigelovii" title="Cylindropuntia bigelovii">Cylindropuntia bigelovii</a></i> in the <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Tree_National_Park" title="Joshua Tree National Park">Joshua Tree National Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Providence_Mountains_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Providence_Mountains_2.jpg/220px-Providence_Mountains_2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Providence_Mountains_2.jpg/330px-Providence_Mountains_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Providence_Mountains_2.jpg/440px-Providence_Mountains_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Providence_Mountains_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mojave_National_Preserve" title="Mojave National Preserve">Mojave National Preserve</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The high elevations of the Canadian zone allow the <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_pine" title="Jeffrey pine">Jeffrey pine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_fir" class="mw-redirect" title="Red fir">red fir</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lodgepole_pine" class="mw-redirect" title="Lodgepole pine">lodgepole pine</a> to thrive. Brushy areas are abundant with dwarf <a href="/wiki/Manzanita" title="Manzanita">manzanita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceanothus" title="Ceanothus">ceanothus</a>; the unique <a href="/wiki/Calvatia_sculpta" title="Calvatia sculpta">Sierra puffball</a> is also found here. Right below the timberline, in the Hudsonian zone, the whitebark, foxtail, and silver pines grow. At about 10,500 feet (3,200&#160;m), begins the Arctic zone, a treeless region whose flora include a number of wildflowers, including <a href="/wiki/Primula_suffrutescens" title="Primula suffrutescens">Sierra primrose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aquilegia_flavescens" title="Aquilegia flavescens">yellow columbine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ranunculus" title="Ranunculus">alpine buttercup</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dodecatheon_alpinum" title="Dodecatheon alpinum">alpine shooting star</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-California:_flora_and_fauna_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Life_Zones_of_the_Central_Sierra_Nevada_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Life_Zones_of_the_Central_Sierra_Nevada-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Common plants that have been introduced to the state include the <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">acacia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schinus" title="Schinus">pepper tree</a>, geranium, and <a href="/wiki/Scotch_broom" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotch broom">Scotch broom</a>. The species that are federally classified as endangered are the <a href="/wiki/Erysimum_capitatum" title="Erysimum capitatum">Contra Costa wallflower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oenothera_deltoides_subsp._howellii" title="Oenothera deltoides subsp. howellii">Antioch Dunes evening primrose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuctoria_mucronata" title="Tuctoria mucronata">Solano grass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delphinium_variegatum" title="Delphinium variegatum">San Clemente Island larkspur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cordylanthus_maritimus" title="Cordylanthus maritimus">salt marsh bird's beak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arabis_blepharophylla" title="Arabis blepharophylla">McDonald's rock-cress</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dudleya_traskiae" title="Dudleya traskiae">Santa Barbara Island liveforever</a>. As of December 1997<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 85 plant species were listed as threatened or endangered.<sup id="cite_ref-California:_flora_and_fauna_80-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the deserts of the lower Sonoran zone, the mammals include the <a href="/wiki/Jackrabbit" class="mw-redirect" title="Jackrabbit">jackrabbit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kangaroo_rat" title="Kangaroo rat">kangaroo rat</a>, squirrel, and opossum. Common birds include the <a href="/wiki/Owl" title="Owl">owl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roadrunner" title="Roadrunner">roadrunner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cactus_wren" title="Cactus wren">cactus wren</a>, and various species of hawk. The area's reptilian life include the <a href="/wiki/Crotalus_cerastes" title="Crotalus cerastes">sidewinder viper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desert_tortoise" title="Desert tortoise">desert tortoise</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Horned_toad" class="mw-redirect" title="Horned toad">horned toad</a>. The upper Sonoran zone boasts mammals such as the <a href="/wiki/Pronghorn" title="Pronghorn">antelope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dusky-footed_woodrat" title="Dusky-footed woodrat">brown-footed woodrat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ring-tailed_cat" title="Ring-tailed cat">ring-tailed cat</a>. Birds unique to this zone are the <a href="/wiki/California_thrasher" title="California thrasher">California thrasher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psaltriparus_minimus" class="mw-redirect" title="Psaltriparus minimus">bushtit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/California_condor" title="California condor">California condor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-California:_flora_and_fauna_80-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-California_Condor_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California_Condor-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CalPhotos:_Browse_Mammal_Common_Names_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CalPhotos:_Browse_Mammal_Common_Names-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Quail_Ridge_Reserve:_UC_Davis_Natural_Reserve_System_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quail_Ridge_Reserve:_UC_Davis_Natural_Reserve_System-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the transition zone, there are Colombian <a href="/wiki/Black-tailed_deer" title="Black-tailed deer">black-tailed deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_black_bear" title="American black bear">black bears</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gray_fox" title="Gray fox">gray foxes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cougar" title="Cougar">cougars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">bobcats</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_elk" title="Roosevelt elk">Roosevelt elk</a>. Reptiles such as the garter snakes and rattlesnakes inhabit the zone. In addition, amphibians such as the <a href="/wiki/Proteidae" title="Proteidae">water puppy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Batrachoseps_attenuatus" class="mw-redirect" title="Batrachoseps attenuatus">redwood salamander</a> are common too. Birds such as the <a href="/wiki/Kingfisher" title="Kingfisher">kingfisher</a>, chickadee, <a href="/wiki/Towhee" title="Towhee">towhee</a>, and hummingbird thrive here as well.<sup id="cite_ref-California:_flora_and_fauna_80-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Black-tailed_Deer_of_California_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black-tailed_Deer_of_California-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Canadian zone mammals include the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_weasel" title="Mountain weasel">mountain weasel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snowshoe_hare" title="Snowshoe hare">snowshoe hare</a>, and several species of chipmunks. Conspicuous birds include the <a href="/wiki/Steller%27s_jay" title="Steller's jay">blue-fronted jay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poecile" title="Poecile">Sierra chickadee</a>. Sierra <a href="/wiki/Hermit_thrush" title="Hermit thrush">hermit thrush</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_ouzel" class="mw-redirect" title="Water ouzel">water ouzel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Townsend%27s_solitaire" title="Townsend's solitaire">Townsend's solitaire</a>. As one ascends into the Hudsonian zone, birds become scarcer. While the Sierra rosy finch is the only bird native to the high Arctic region, other bird species such as the hummingbird and <a href="/wiki/Clark%27s_nutcracker" title="Clark's nutcracker">Clark's nutcracker</a>. Principal mammals found in this region include the Sierra coney, <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_jackrabbit" title="White-tailed jackrabbit">white-tailed jackrabbit</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bighorn_sheep" title="Bighorn sheep">bighorn sheep</a>. As of April 2003<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the bighorn sheep was listed as endangered by the US Fish and Wildlife Service. The fauna found throughout several zones are the <a href="/wiki/Mule_deer" title="Mule deer">mule deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coyote" title="Coyote">coyote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_lion" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain lion">mountain lion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_flicker" title="Northern flicker">northern flicker</a>, and several species of hawk and sparrow.<sup id="cite_ref-California:_flora_and_fauna_80-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aquatic life in California thrives, from the state's mountain lakes and streams to the rocky Pacific coastline. Numerous trout species are found, among them <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_trout" title="Rainbow trout">rainbow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_trout" title="Golden trout">golden</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cutthroat_trout" title="Cutthroat trout">cutthroat</a>. Migratory species of salmon are common as well. Deep-sea life forms include <a href="/wiki/White_seabass" title="White seabass">sea bass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellowfin_tuna" title="Yellowfin tuna">yellowfin tuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barracuda" title="Barracuda">barracuda</a>, and several types of whale. Native to the cliffs of northern California are seals, sea lions, and many types of shorebirds, including migratory species.<sup id="cite_ref-California:_flora_and_fauna_80-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of April 2003, 118 California animals were on the federal endangered list; 181 plants were listed as endangered or threatened. Endangered animals include the <a href="/wiki/Vulpes_macrotis" class="mw-redirect" title="Vulpes macrotis">San Joaquin kitfox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aplodontia_rufa_nigra" class="mw-redirect" title="Aplodontia rufa nigra">Point Arena mountain beaver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pacific_pocket_mouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific pocket mouse">Pacific pocket mouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt_marsh_harvest_mouse" title="Salt marsh harvest mouse">salt marsh harvest mouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morro_Bay_kangaroo_rat" title="Morro Bay kangaroo rat">Morro Bay kangaroo rat</a> (and five other species of kangaroo rat), <a href="/wiki/California_vole#Subspecies" title="California vole">Amargosa vole</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_least_tern" title="California least tern">California least tern</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_condor" title="California condor">California condor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loggerhead_shrike" title="Loggerhead shrike">loggerhead shrike</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bell%27s_sparrow" title="Bell's sparrow">San Clemente sage sparrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_garter_snake" title="San Francisco garter snake">San Francisco garter snake</a>, five species of salamander, three species of chub, and two species of pupfish. Eleven butterflies are also endangered<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and two that are threatened are on the federal list.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Among threatened animals are the coastal <a href="/wiki/California_gnatcatcher" title="California gnatcatcher">California gnatcatcher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paiute_cutthroat_trout" title="Paiute cutthroat trout">Paiute cutthroat trout</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_otter#Subspecies" title="Sea otter">southern sea otter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_spotted_owl" title="Northern spotted owl">northern spotted owl</a>. California has a total of 290,821 acres (1,176.91&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of National Wildlife Refuges.<sup id="cite_ref-California:_flora_and_fauna_80-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California:_flora_and_fauna-80">[80]</a></sup> As of September 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 123 California animals were listed as either endangered or threatened on the federal list provided by the <a href="/wiki/US_Fish_%26_Wildlife_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="US Fish &amp; Wildlife Service">US Fish &amp; Wildlife Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._Fish_.26_Wildlife_Service:_Species_Reports:_Listings_and_occurrences_for_California_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Fish_.26_Wildlife_Service:_Species_Reports:_Listings_and_occurrences_for_California-88">[88]</a></sup> Also, as of the same year<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 178 species of California plants were listed either as endangered or threatened on this federal list.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._Fish_.26_Wildlife_Service:_Species_Reports:_Listings_and_occurrences_for_California_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._Fish_.26_Wildlife_Service:_Species_Reports:_Listings_and_occurrences_for_California-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivers">Rivers</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_California" title="List of rivers of California">List of rivers of California</a></div>
<p>The vast majority of rivers in California are dammed as part of two massive water projects: the <a href="/wiki/Central_Valley_Project" title="Central Valley Project">Central Valley Project</a>, providing water to the agricultural central valley, the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Water_Project" title="California State Water Project">California State Water Project</a> diverting water from northern to southern California. The state's coasts, rivers, and other bodies of water are regulated by the <a href="/wiki/California_Coastal_Commission" title="California Coastal Commission">California Coastal Commission</a>.</p>
<p>The two most prominent rivers within California are the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_River" title="Sacramento River">Sacramento River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_River" title="San Joaquin River">San Joaquin River</a>, which drain the Central Valley and the west slope of the Sierra Nevada and flow to the Pacific Ocean through <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay" title="San Francisco Bay">San Francisco Bay</a>. Several major tributaries feed into the Sacramento and the San Joaquin, including the <a href="/wiki/Pit_River" title="Pit River">Pit River</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tuolumne_River" title="Tuolumne River">Tuolumne River</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Feather_River" title="Feather River">Feather River</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Eel_River_(California)" title="Eel River (California)">Eel River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salinas_River_(California)" title="Salinas River (California)">Salinas River</a> each drain portions of the California coast, north and south of San Francisco Bay, respectively, and the Eel River is the largest river in the state to remain in its natural un-dammed state. The <a href="/wiki/Mojave_River" title="Mojave River">Mojave River</a> is the primary watercourse in the Mojave Desert, and the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_River" title="Santa Ana River">Santa Ana River</a> drains much of the <a href="/wiki/Transverse_Ranges" title="Transverse Ranges">Transverse Ranges</a> as it bisects Southern California. Some other important rivers are the <a href="/wiki/Klamath_River" title="Klamath River">Klamath River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Trinity_River_(California)" title="Trinity River (California)">Trinity River</a> in the far north coast, and the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a> on the southeast border with <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>.</p>

before declining to 15,000 by 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-PopEst_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopEst-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cabrillo1_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cabrillo1-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-americanindiantah1_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-americanindiantah1-92">[92]</a></sup></td>

</table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of California was 39,144,818 on July 1, 2015, a 5.08% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PopEst_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopEst-4">[4]</a></sup> Between 2000 and 2009, there was a natural increase of 3,090,016 (5,058,440 births minus 2,179,958 deaths).<sup id="cite_ref-popEstChanges_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popEstChanges-93">[93]</a></sup> During this time period, <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">international migration</a> produced a net increase of 1,816,633 people while domestic migration produced a net decrease of 1,509,708, resulting in a net in-migration of 306,925 people.<sup id="cite_ref-popEstChanges_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popEstChanges-93">[93]</a></sup> The state of California's own statistics show a population of 38,292,687 for January 1, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-CA_popEst_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CA_popEst-94">[94]</a></sup> However, according to the <a href="/wiki/Manhattan_Institute_for_Policy_Research" title="Manhattan Institute for Policy Research">Manhattan Institute for Policy Research</a>, since 1990 almost 3.4 million Californians have moved to other states, with most leaving to Texas, Nevada, and Arizona.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>California is the 2nd-most populous subnational entity in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a> and the Americas, with a population second to that of the state of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a> in Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-Resultados_do_Censo_2010_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Resultados_do_Censo_2010-96">[96]</a></sup> California's population is greater than that of all but 34 countries of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Global_popEst_USCensus_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_popEst_USCensus-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Global_popEst_UN_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_popEst_UN-98">[98]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Area" title="Greater Los Angeles Area">Greater Los Angeles Area</a> is the 2nd-largest <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> in the United States, after the <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York metropolitan area</a>, while Los Angeles, with nearly half the population of New York, is the 2nd-largest city in the United States. Also, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles County">Los Angeles County</a> has held the title of most populous United States county for decades, and it alone is more populous than 42 United States states.<sup id="cite_ref-LA_County_DPSS_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA_County_DPSS-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Baby_Slump_In_L.A._County_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baby_Slump_In_L.A._County-100">[100]</a></sup> Including Los Angeles, four of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">top 15 most populous cities in the U.S.</a> are in California: Los Angeles (2nd), San Diego (8th), San Jose (10th), and San Francisco (13th). The <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> of California is located in the town of <a href="/wiki/Buttonwillow,_California" title="Buttonwillow, California">Buttonwillow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kern_County,_California" title="Kern County, California">Kern County</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[note 1]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_centers">Population centers</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_California" title="List of cities and towns in California">List of cities and towns in California</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_California_cities_by_population" title="List of largest California cities by population">List of largest California cities by population</a></div>
<p>The state has 482 <a href="/wiki/Municipal_corporation" title="Municipal corporation">incorporated</a> cities and towns; of which 460 are cities and 22 are towns. Under California law, the terms "city" and "town" are explicitly interchangeable; the name of an incorporated municipality in the state can either be "City of (Name)" or "Town of (Name)".<sup id="cite_ref-Cal_Gov_Code_34502_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cal_Gov_Code_34502-103">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento</a> became California's first incorporated city on February 27, 1850.<sup id="cite_ref-Sacramento_Charter_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sacramento_Charter-104">[103]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose</a>, San Diego and <a href="/wiki/Benicia,_California" title="Benicia, California">Benicia</a> tied for California's second incorporated city, each receiving incorporation on March 27, 1850.<sup id="cite_ref-San_Jose_Inc_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-San_Jose_Inc-105">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_of_San_Diego_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_San_Diego-106">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Benicia_Inc_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benicia_Inc-107">[106]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jurupa_Valley,_California" title="Jurupa Valley, California">Jurupa Valley</a> became the state's most recent and 482nd incorporated municipality on July 1, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>The majority of these cities and towns are within one of five <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan areas</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles Metropolitan Area">Los Angeles Metropolitan Area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Riverside-San_Bernardino_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Riverside-San Bernardino Area">Riverside-San Bernardino Area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego metropolitan area">San Diego metropolitan area</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento_metropolitan_area" title="Sacramento metropolitan area">Sacramento metropolitan area</a>.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Migration">Migration</span></h4>
<p>Starting in the year 2010, for the first time since the <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">California Gold Rush</a>, California-born residents make up the majority of the state's population.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> Along with the rest of the United States, California's immigration pattern has also shifted over the course of the late 2000s-early 2010s.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Mexican_Immigration_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Mexican_Immigration-112">[111]</a></sup> Immigration from <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin American</a> countries has dropped significantly with most immigrants now coming from <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SacBee17JAN2013_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SacBee17JAN2013-113">[112]</a></sup> In total for 2011, there were 277,304 immigrants. 57% came from Asian countries vs. 22% from Latin American countries.<sup id="cite_ref-SacBee17JAN2013_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SacBee17JAN2013-113">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Net_immigration" class="mw-redirect" title="Net immigration">Net immigration</a> from Mexico, previously the most common country of origin for new immigrants has dropped to zero/less than zero, since more Mexican nationals are departing for their home country than immigrating.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Mexican_Immigration_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Mexican_Immigration-112">[111]</a></sup> As a result it is estimated that Hispanic citizens will constitute 49% of the population by 2060, instead of the previously projected 2050, due primarily to domestic births.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Mexican_Immigration_112-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Mexican_Immigration-112">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Economist_CA_Hispanics_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist_CA_Hispanics-114">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state's population of <a href="/wiki/Undocumented_immigrants" class="mw-redirect" title="Undocumented immigrants">undocumented immigrants</a> has been shrinking in recent years, due to increased enforcement and decreased job opportunities for lower-skilled workers.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> The number of migrants arrested attempting to cross the Mexican border in the Southwest plunged from a high of 1.1 million in 2005 to just 367,000 in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-BusinessWeek_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusinessWeek-116">[115]</a></sup> Despite these recent trends, <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigration to the United States">illegal</a> <a href="/wiki/Alien_(law)" title="Alien (law)">aliens</a> constituted an estimated 7.3 percent of the state's population, the third highest percentage of any state in the <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigrant_population_of_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigrant population of the United States">country</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[note 2]</a></sup> totaling nearly 2.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-SDUT19042011_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDUT19042011-119">[117]</a></sup> In particular, illegal immigrants tended to be concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County,_California" title="Los Angeles County, California">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monterey_County,_California" title="Monterey County, California">Monterey</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Benito_County,_California" title="San Benito County, California">San Benito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_County,_California" title="Imperial County, California">Imperial</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Napa_County,_California" title="Napa County, California">Napa</a> Counties – the latter four of which have significant agricultural industries that depend on manual labor.<sup id="cite_ref-PPIC2011II_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PPIC2011II-120">[118]</a></sup> More than half of illegal immigrants originate from Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-SDUT19042011_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDUT19042011-119">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT">LGBT</span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_California" title="LGBT rights in California">LGBT rights in California</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_history_in_California" title="LGBT history in California">LGBT history in California</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CACourt_protest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/CACourt_protest.jpg/180px-CACourt_protest.jpg" width="180" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/CACourt_protest.jpg/270px-CACourt_protest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/CACourt_protest.jpg/360px-CACourt_protest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="2524" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CACourt_protest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pro- and anti-<a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_8" class="mw-redirect" title="California Proposition 8">Proposition 8</a> protesters clash at a rally in front of San Francisco City Hall.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>California is considered generally liberal in <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_California" title="LGBT rights in California">its policies</a> regarding the <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> community, and the rights of lesbian, gay, bisexual, and transgender people have received greater recognition since 1960 at both the state and municipal level. California is home to a number of <a href="/wiki/Gay_village" title="Gay village">gay villages</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Castro_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Castro District">Castro District</a> in San Francisco, <a href="/wiki/Hillcrest,_San_Diego" title="Hillcrest, San Diego">Hillcrest</a> in San Diego, and <a href="/wiki/West_Hollywood" class="mw-redirect" title="West Hollywood">West Hollywood</a>. Through the Domestic Partnership Act of 1999, California became the first state in the United States to recognize same-sex relationships in any legal capacity. In 2000, voters passed <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_22_(2000)" title="California Proposition 22 (2000)">Proposition 22</a>, which restricted state recognition of marriage to opposite-sex couples. This was struck down by the <a href="/wiki/California_Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="California Supreme Court">California Supreme Court</a> in May 2008, effectively legalizing same-sex marriage; however, this was overruled later that same year when California voters passed <a href="/wiki/Proposition_8" class="mw-redirect" title="Proposition 8">Proposition 8</a>. After further judicial cases, in 2013 the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Supreme Court">U.S. Supreme Court</a> <a href="/wiki/Hollingsworth_v._Perry" title="Hollingsworth v. Perry">rendered the law void</a>, allowing same-sex marriages in California to resume.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_origins">National origins</span></h3>
<p>According to the United States Census Bureau in 2015 the population self-identifies as (alone or in combination):<sup id="cite_ref-2015CensusDemo_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015CensusDemo-121">[119]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>72.9% <a href="/wiki/White_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White American">White</a></li>
<li>14.7% <a href="/wiki/Asian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian American">Asian</a></li>
<li>6.5% Black or <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African American</a></li>
<li>3.8% <a href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiracial American">Two or More Races</a></li>
<li>1.7% <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Native" class="mw-redirect" title="Alaska Native">Alaska Native</a></li>
<li>0.5% <a href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiian" class="mw-redirect" title="Native Hawaiian">Native Hawaiian</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islander American">Pacific Islander</a></li>
</ul>
<p>By ethnicity, in 2015 the population was 61.2% non-Hispanic (of any race) and 38.8% <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic or Latino</a> (of any race).<sup id="cite_ref-2015CensusDemo_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015CensusDemo-121">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2011, 75.1% of California's population younger than age 1 were minorities, meaning that they had at least one parent who was not non-Hispanic white (white Hispanics are counted as minorities).<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>In terms of total numbers, California has the largest population of White Americans in the United States, an estimated 22,200,000 residents. The state has the 5th largest population of African Americans in the United States, an estimated 2,250,000 residents. California's Asian American population is estimated at 4.4 million, constituting a third of the nation's total. California's Native American population of 285,000 is the most of any state.<sup id="cite_ref-US_Census_Cal_Race_and_Ethnicity_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_Census_Cal_Race_and_Ethnicity-123">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to estimates from 2011, California has the largest <a href="/wiki/Majority-minority_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Majority-minority state">minority population</a> in the United States by numbers, making up 60% of the state population.<sup id="cite_ref-CensusQuickFacts_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CensusQuickFacts-91">[91]</a></sup> Over the past 25 years, the population of <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites" title="Non-Hispanic whites">non-Hispanic whites</a> has declined, while <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanic and Latino American">Hispanic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian American">Asian</a> populations have grown. Between 1970 and 2011, non-Hispanic whites declined from 80% of the State's population to 40%, while <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispanic and Latino American">Hispanics</a> grew from 32% in 2000 to 38% in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> It is currently projected that Hispanics will rise to 49% of the population by 2060, primarily due to domestic births rather than immigration.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist_CA_Hispanics_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist_CA_Hispanics-114">[113]</a></sup> With the decline of immigration from Latin America, Asian Americans now constitute the fastest growing racial/ethnic group in California; this growth primarily driven by immigration from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Asians_CA_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asians_CA-125">[123]</a></sup></p>

<p><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">English</a> serves as California's <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a> and <a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a> <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>. In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Modern_Language_Association_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Modern Language Association of America">Modern Language Association of America</a> estimated that 57.02% (19,429,309) of California residents age 5 and older spoke only <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> at home, while 42.98% spoke another <a href="/wiki/Primary_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary language">primary language</a> at home. According to the 2007 <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">American Community Survey</a>, 73% of people who speak a language other than English at home are able to speak English well or very well, with 9.8% not speaking English at all.<sup id="cite_ref-Language2007_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Language2007-2">[2]</a></sup> Like most <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">U.S. states</a> (32 out of 50), California law enshrines English as its <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>, and has done so since the passage of <a href="/wiki/List_of_California_ballot_propositions_1980%E2%80%931989#November_4.2C_1986" class="mw-redirect" title="List of California ballot propositions 1980–1989">Proposition 63</a> by California voters. Various government agencies do, and are often required to, furnish documents in the various languages needed to reach their intended audiences.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AB_800_Analysis_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AB_800_Analysis-138">[130]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hull_English_already_official_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hull_English_already_official-139">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>In total, 16 languages other than English were spoken as primary languages at home by more than 100,000 persons, more than any other state in the nation. New York State, in second place, had 9 languages other than English spoken by more than 100,000 persons.<sup id="cite_ref-MLA_Data_Center_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLA_Data_Center-140">[132]</a></sup> The most common language spoken besides English was <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, spoken by 28.46% (9,696,638) of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist_CA_Hispanics_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist_CA_Hispanics-114">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pew_Mexican_Immigration_112-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew_Mexican_Immigration-112">[111]</a></sup> With Asia contributing most of California's new immigrants, California had the highest concentration nationwide of <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> speakers, the second highest concentration of <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, and the third highest concentration of <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a> speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-Language2007_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Language2007-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>California has historically been one of the most linguistically diverse areas in the world, with more than 70 indigenous languages derived from 64 root languages in 6 language families.<sup id="cite_ref-Native_Languages_1770_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Native_Languages_1770-141">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Indian_Root_Languages_1994_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Indian_Root_Languages_1994-142">[134]</a></sup> A survey conducted between 2007 and 2009 identified 23 different indigenous languages of Mexico that are spoken among California farmworkers.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[135]</a></sup> All of California's indigenous languages are <a href="/wiki/Endangered_language" title="Endangered language">endangered</a>, although there are now efforts toward <a href="/wiki/Language_revitalization" title="Language revitalization">language revitalization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-indigenous_languages_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indigenous_languages-144">[note 3]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a result of the state's increasing diversity and migration from other areas across the country and around the globe, linguists began noticing a noteworthy set of emerging characteristics of spoken English in California since the late 20th century. This dialect, known as <a href="/wiki/California_English" title="California English">California English</a>, has a <a href="/wiki/Vowel_shift" title="Vowel shift">vowel shift</a> and several other phonological processes that are different from the dialects used in other regions of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Bucholtz_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bucholtz-145">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_California" title="Culture of California">Culture of California</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hollywood_Sign_(Zuschnitt).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/220px-Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/330px-Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/440px-Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="11065" data-file-height="6916" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hollywood_Sign_(Zuschnitt).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Sign" title="Hollywood Sign">Hollywood Sign</a>, a symbol of the American film industry</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The culture of California is a Western culture and most clearly has its modern roots in the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States" title="Culture of the United States">culture of the United States</a>, but also, historically, many <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> influences. As a border and coastal state, Californian culture has been greatly influenced by several large immigrant populations, especially those from Latin America and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-World_of_Opportunity_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_of_Opportunity-146">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>California has long been a subject of interest in the public mind and has often been promoted by its boosters as a kind of paradise. In the early 20th century, fueled by the efforts of state and local boosters, many Americans saw the Golden State as an ideal resort destination, sunny and dry all year round with easy access to the ocean and mountains. In the 1960s, popular music groups such as <a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys" title="The Beach Boys">The Beach Boys</a> promoted the image of Californians as laid-back, tanned beach-goers.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">California Gold Rush</a> of the 1850s is <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush#Longer-term_effects" title="California Gold Rush">still seen as a symbol of California's economic style</a>, which tends to generate technology, social, entertainment, and economic fads and booms and related busts.</p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:San-diego-mission-church.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/San-diego-mission-church.JPG/220px-San-diego-mission-church.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/San-diego-mission-church.JPG/330px-San-diego-mission-church.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/San-diego-mission-church.JPG/440px-San-diego-mission-church.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:San-diego-mission-church.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mission_San_Diego_de_Alcal%C3%A1" title="Mission San Diego de Alcalá">Mission San Diego de Alcalá</a>, one of the first <a href="/wiki/Spanish_missions_in_California" title="Spanish missions in California">Spanish missions in California</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The largest religious denominations by number of adherents as a percentage of California's population in 2014 were the Catholic Church with 28 percent, Evangelical Protestants with 20 percent, and Mainline Protestants with 10 percent. Together, all kinds of Protestants accounted for 32 percent. Those unaffiliated with any religion represented 27 percent of the population. The breakdown of other religions is 1% Muslim, 2% Hindu and 2% Buddhist.<sup id="cite_ref-pew2014_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew2014-147">[138]</a></sup> This is a change from 2008, when the population identified their religion with the Catholic Church with 31 percent; Evangelical Protestants with 18 percent; and Mainline Protestants with 14 percent. In 2008, those unaffiliated with any religion represented 21 percent of the population. The breakdown of other religions in 2008 was 0.5% Muslim, 1% Hindu and 2% Buddhist.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[139]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/American_Jewish_Year_Book" title="American Jewish Year Book">American Jewish Year Book</a></i> placed the total <a href="/wiki/American_Jews" title="American Jews">Jewish</a> population of California at about 1,194,190 in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[140]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">Association of Religion Data Archives</a> (ARDA) the largest denominations by adherents in 2010 were the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> with 10,233,334; <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> with 763,818; and the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Southern Baptist Convention</a> with 489,953.<sup id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-150">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first priests to come to California were Roman Catholic missionaries from Spain. Roman Catholics founded <a href="/wiki/California_missions" class="mw-redirect" title="California missions">21 missions along the California coast</a>, as well as the cities of Los Angeles and San Francisco. California continues to have a large Roman Catholic population due to the large numbers of Mexicans and Central Americans living within its borders. California has twelve dioceses and two archdioceses, the <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Los_Angeles" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese of Los Angeles">Archdiocese of Los Angeles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_San_Francisco" class="mw-redirect" title="Archdiocese of San Francisco">Archdiocese of San Francisco</a>, the former being the largest archdiocese in the United States.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> survey revealed that California is somewhat less religious than the rest of the US: 62 percent of Californians say they are "absolutely certain" of their belief in God, while in the nation 71 percent say so. The survey also revealed 48 percent of Californians say religion is "very important", compared to 56 percent nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-Helfland_2008_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Helfland_2008-151">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_California" title="Sports in California">Sports in California</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_professional_sports_teams_in_California" title="List of professional sports teams in California">List of professional sports teams in California</a></div>
<p>California has twenty <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_league" class="mw-redirect" title="Major professional sports league">major professional sports league</a> franchises, far more than any other state. The <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a> has seven major league teams spread in its three major cities: San Francisco, San Jose, and Oakland. While the Greater Los Angeles Area is home to ten major league franchises. San Diego and Sacramento each have one major league team. The NFL <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> has been hosted in California 11 times at four different stadiums: <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Memorial_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum">Los Angeles Memorial Coliseum</a>, the Rose Bowl, Stanford Stadium, and San Diego's <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm_Stadium" title="Qualcomm Stadium">Qualcomm Stadium</a>. A twelfth, <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_50" title="Super Bowl 50">Super Bowl 50</a>, was held at <a href="/wiki/Levi%27s_Stadium" title="Levi's Stadium">Levi's Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara,_California" title="Santa Clara, California">Santa Clara</a> on February 7, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>California has long had many respected collegiate sports programs. California is home to the oldest college bowl game, the annual <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl</a>, among others.</p>
<p>California is the only US state to have hosted both the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter</a> Olympics. The <a href="/wiki/1932_Summer_Olympics" title="1932 Summer Olympics">1932</a> and <a href="/wiki/1984_Summer_Olympics" title="1984 Summer Olympics">1984 Summer Olympics</a> were held in Los Angeles. <a href="/wiki/Squaw_Valley_Ski_Resort" title="Squaw Valley Ski Resort">Squaw Valley Ski Resort</a> in the Lake Tahoe region hosted the <a href="/wiki/1960_Winter_Olympics" title="1960 Winter Olympics">1960 Winter Olympics</a>. Multiple games during the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 FIFA World Cup</a> took place in California, with the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Rose Bowl Stadium">Rose Bowl</a> hosting eight matches including the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1994 FIFA World Cup Final">final</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Stadium" title="Stanford Stadium">Stanford Stadium</a> hosted six matches.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LA_Coliseum_gate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/LA_Coliseum_gate.jpg/170px-LA_Coliseum_gate.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/LA_Coliseum_gate.jpg/255px-LA_Coliseum_gate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/LA_Coliseum_gate.jpg/340px-LA_Coliseum_gate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a>

</div>
</div>
