<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:THS_facade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/THS_facade.jpg/220px-THS_facade.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/THS_facade.jpg/330px-THS_facade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/THS_facade.jpg/440px-THS_facade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:THS_facade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Torrance_High_School" title="Torrance High School">Torrance High School</a> is one of the oldest high schools in continuous use in California and a popular location for television and motion picture production.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_California" title="Education in California">Education in California</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_California" title="List of colleges and universities in California">List of colleges and universities in California</a></div>
<p>Public <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education_in_the_United_States" title="Secondary education in the United States">secondary education</a> consists of <a href="/wiki/High_school#United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="High school">high schools</a> that teach elective courses in trades, languages, and liberal arts with tracks for gifted, college-bound and industrial arts students. California's public educational system is supported by a <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_98_(1988)" title="California Proposition 98 (1988)">unique constitutional amendment</a> that requires a minimum annual funding level for grades K–12 and <a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">community colleges</a> that grows with the economy and student enrollment figures.<sup id="cite_ref-Prop_98_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prop_98-153">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>California had over 6.2 million school students in the 2005–06 school year. Funding and staffing levels in California schools lag behind other states. In expenditure per pupil, California ranked 29th (of the 50 states and the <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">District of Columbia</a>) in 2005–06. In teaching staff expenditure per pupil, California ranked 49th of 51. In overall teacher-pupil ratio, California was also 49th, with 21 students per teacher. Only Arizona and Utah were lower.<sup id="cite_ref-How_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-How-154">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2007 study concluded that California's public school system was "broken" in that it suffered from over-regulation.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>California's public <a href="/wiki/Postsecondary_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Postsecondary education">postsecondary education</a> offers three separate systems:</p>
<ul>
<li>The research university system in the state is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> (UC), a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public university</a> system. As of fall 2011, the University of California had a combined <a href="/wiki/Student" title="Student">student</a> body of 234,464 students.<sup id="cite_ref-About_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About-156">[147]</a></sup> There are ten general UC campuses, and a number of specialized campuses in the UC system. The system was originally intended to accept the top one-eighth of California high school students, but several of the schools have become even more selective.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The UC system was originally given exclusive authority in awarding Ph.Ds, but this has since changed and the CSU is also able to award several Doctoral degrees.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/California_State_University" title="California State University">California State University</a> (CSU) system has almost 430,000 students, making it the largest university system in the United States. The CSU was originally intended to accept the top one-third of California high school students, but several of the schools have become much more selective.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The CSU was originally set up to award only bachelor's and master's degrees, but has since been granted the authority to award several Doctoral degrees.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/California_Community_Colleges_System" title="California Community Colleges System">California Community Colleges System</a> provides lower division coursework as well as basic skills and workforce training. It is the largest network of higher education in the US, composed of 112 colleges serving a student population of over 2.6 million.</li>
</ul>
<p>California is also home to such notable private universities as <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a>, the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">California Institute of Technology</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Claremont_Colleges" title="Claremont Colleges">Claremont Colleges</a>. California has hundreds of other private colleges and universities, including many religious and special-purpose institutions.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_California" title="Economy of California">Economy of California</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/California_locations_by_per_capita_income" class="mw-redirect" title="California locations by per capita income">California locations by per capita income</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gross_Domestic_Product_of_California_2008_(millions_of_current_dollars).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gross_Domestic_Product_of_California_2008_%28millions_of_current_dollars%29.svg/350px-Gross_Domestic_Product_of_California_2008_%28millions_of_current_dollars%29.svg.png" width="350" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gross_Domestic_Product_of_California_2008_%28millions_of_current_dollars%29.svg/525px-Gross_Domestic_Product_of_California_2008_%28millions_of_current_dollars%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gross_Domestic_Product_of_California_2008_%28millions_of_current_dollars%29.svg/700px-Gross_Domestic_Product_of_California_2008_%28millions_of_current_dollars%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="690" data-file-height="490" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gross_Domestic_Product_of_California_2008_(millions_of_current_dollars).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gross Domestic Product of California by sector for 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-BEA2_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BEA2-157">[148]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USA-World_Nominal_GDP.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/USA-World_Nominal_GDP.PNG/350px-USA-World_Nominal_GDP.PNG" width="350" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/USA-World_Nominal_GDP.PNG/525px-USA-World_Nominal_GDP.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/USA-World_Nominal_GDP.PNG/700px-USA-World_Nominal_GDP.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1407" data-file-height="663" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USA-World_Nominal_GDP.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Had California been an independent country in 2008 its gross domestic product would have been ranked <a href="/wiki/Comparison_between_U.S._states_and_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="Comparison between U.S. states and countries by GDP (PPP)">between eighth and eleventh</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Country_Comparison_GDP_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_Country_Comparison_GDP-158">[149]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The economy of California is large enough to be comparable to that of the largest of countries. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Gross_state_product" title="Gross state product">gross state product</a> (GSP) is about $2.514 <a href="/wiki/1000000000000_(number)" class="mw-redirect" title="1000000000000 (number)">trillion</a>, the largest in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-gdp-by-state_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdp-by-state-159">[150]</a></sup> California is responsible for 13.9 percent of the United States' approximate $18.1 trillion gross domestic product (GDP).<sup id="cite_ref-gdp-by-state_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gdp-by-state-159">[150]</a></sup> California's GSP is larger than the GDP of all but 5 countries in dollar terms (the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ccsce_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccsce-161">[152]</a></sup> larger than Brazil, France, Russia, Italy, India, Canada, Australia, Spain and Turkey. In <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_Power_Parity" class="mw-redirect" title="Purchasing Power Parity">Purchasing Power Parity</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8large_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8large-162">[153]</a></sup> it is larger than all but 10 countries (the United States, China, India, Japan, Germany, Russia, Brazil, France, the United Kingdom, and Indonesia), larger than Italy, Mexico, Spain, South Korea, Saudi Arabia, Canada and Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank2012_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank2012-163">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>The five largest sectors of employment in California are trade, transportation, and utilities; government; professional and business services; education and health services; and leisure and hospitality. In output, the five largest sectors are financial services, followed by trade, transportation, and utilities; education and health services; government; and manufacturing.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[155]</a></sup> As of September 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, California has an <a href="/wiki/California_unemployment_statistics" title="California unemployment statistics">unemployment</a> rate of 5.5%.</p>
<p>California's economy is dependent on trade and international related commerce accounts for about one-quarter of the state's economy. In 2008, California exported $144 billion worth of goods, up from $134 billion in 2007 and $127 billion in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-Cal_Trade_Statistics_2008_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cal_Trade_Statistics_2008-165">[156]</a></sup> Computers and electronic products are California's top export, accounting for 42 percent of all the state's exports in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Cal_Trade_Statistics_2008_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cal_Trade_Statistics_2008-165">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>Agriculture is an important sector in California's economy. Farming-related sales more than quadrupled over the past three decades, from $7.3 billion in 1974 to nearly $31 billion in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-Cal_Facts_2006_State_Economy_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cal_Facts_2006_State_Economy-166">[157]</a></sup> This increase has occurred despite a 15 percent decline in acreage devoted to farming during the period, and water supply suffering from chronic instability. Factors contributing to the growth in sales-per-acre include more intensive use of active farmlands and technological improvements in crop production.<sup id="cite_ref-Cal_Facts_2006_State_Economy_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cal_Facts_2006_State_Economy-166">[157]</a></sup> In 2008, California's 81,500 farms and ranches generated $36.2 billion products revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-California_Agricultural_Production_Statistics_2009.E2.80.932010_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California_Agricultural_Production_Statistics_2009.E2.80.932010-167">[158]</a></sup> In 2011, that number grew to $43.5 billion products revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-California_Agricultural_Production_Statistics_2011_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-California_Agricultural_Production_Statistics_2011-168">[159]</a></sup> The Agriculture sector accounts for two percent of the state's GDP and employs around three percent of its total workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[160]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">USDA</a> in 2011, the three largest California agricultural products by value were <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cream" title="Cream">cream</a>, shelled <a href="/wiki/Almonds" class="mw-redirect" title="Almonds">almonds</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grapes" class="mw-redirect" title="Grapes">grapes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_GDP_per_capita" title="List of U.S. states by GDP per capita">Per capita GDP</a> in 2007 was $38,956, ranking eleventh in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-BEA_State_Personal_Income_2006_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BEA_State_Personal_Income_2006-171">[162]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/California_locations_by_per_capita_income" class="mw-redirect" title="California locations by per capita income">Per capita income</a> varies widely by geographic region and profession. The Central Valley is the most impoverished, with <a href="/wiki/Migrant_worker" title="Migrant worker">migrant farm workers</a> making less than <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a>. According to a 2005 report by the <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Research_Service" title="Congressional Research Service">Congressional Research Service</a>, the <a href="/wiki/San_Joaquin_Valley" title="San Joaquin Valley">San Joaquin Valley</a> was characterized as one of the most economically depressed regions in the United States, on par with the region of <a href="/wiki/Appalachia" title="Appalachia">Appalachia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CRS_San_Joaquin_Valley_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CRS_San_Joaquin_Valley-172">[163]</a></sup> California has a <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_the_United_States" title="Poverty in the United States">poverty rate</a> of 23.5%, the highest of any state in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[164]</a></sup> Many coastal cities include some of the wealthiest per-capita areas in the United States The high-technology sectors in Northern California, specifically <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_County,_California" title="Santa Clara County, California">Santa Clara</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Mateo_County,_California" title="San Mateo County, California">San Mateo counties</a>, have emerged from the economic downturn caused by the <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">dot-com bust</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_Map_of_Occupations_by_Share_in_California_(2014).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Tree_Map_of_Occupations_by_Share_in_California_%282014%29.png/220px-Tree_Map_of_Occupations_by_Share_in_California_%282014%29.png" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Tree_Map_of_Occupations_by_Share_in_California_%282014%29.png/330px-Tree_Map_of_Occupations_by_Share_in_California_%282014%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Tree_Map_of_Occupations_by_Share_in_California_%282014%29.png/440px-Tree_Map_of_Occupations_by_Share_in_California_%282014%29.png 2x" data-file-width="2320" data-file-height="1362" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_Map_of_Occupations_by_Share_in_California_(2014).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A tree map depicting the distribution of occupations across the state of California</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2010, there were more than 663,000 millionaires in the state, more than any other state in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[165]</a></sup> In 2010, California residents were ranked first among the states with the best average credit score of 754.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[166]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_finances">State finances</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/California_state_finances" title="California state finances">California state finances</a> and <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9312_California_budget_crisis" title="2008–12 California budget crisis">2008–12 California budget crisis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:California_economic_regions_map_(labeled_and_colored).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/California_economic_regions_map_%28labeled_and_colored%29.svg/220px-California_economic_regions_map_%28labeled_and_colored%29.svg.png" width="220" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/California_economic_regions_map_%28labeled_and_colored%29.svg/330px-California_economic_regions_map_%28labeled_and_colored%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/California_economic_regions_map_%28labeled_and_colored%29.svg/440px-California_economic_regions_map_%28labeled_and_colored%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="621" data-file-height="733" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:California_economic_regions_map_(labeled_and_colored).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Economic_regions_of_California" title="Economic regions of California">Economic regions of California</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>State spending increased from $56 billion in 1998 to $127 billion in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[168]</a></sup> California, with 12% of the United States population, has one-third of the nation's <a href="/wiki/Social_programs_in_the_United_States" title="Social programs in the United States">welfare</a> recipients.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[169]</a></sup> California has the third highest per capita spending on welfare among the states, as well as the highest spending on welfare at $6.67 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[170]</a></sup> In January 2011 the California's total debt was at least $265 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[171]</a></sup> On June 27, 2013, Governor Jerry Brown signed a balanced budget (no deficit) for the state, its first in decades; however the state's debt remains at $132 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the passage of <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_30_(2012)" class="mw-redirect" title="California Proposition 30 (2012)">Proposition 30 in 2012</a>, California now levies a 13.3% maximum marginal <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a> rate with ten <a href="/wiki/Tax_bracket" title="Tax bracket">tax brackets</a>, ranging from 1% at the bottom tax bracket of $0 annual individual income to 13.3% for annual individual income over $1,000,000. California has a <a href="/wiki/Sales_taxes_in_the_United_States#California" title="Sales taxes in the United States">state sales tax</a> of 7.5%, though local governments can and do levy additional sales taxes. Many of these taxes are temporary for a seven-year period (as stipulated in Proposition 30) and afterwards will revert to a previous maximum marginal income tax bracket of 10.3% and state sales tax rate of 7.25%.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>All <a href="/wiki/Real_property" title="Real property">real property</a> is taxable annually; the tax is based on the property's fair market value at the time of purchase or new construction. Property tax increases are capped at 2% per year (see <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_13_(1978)" title="California Proposition 13 (1978)">Proposition 13</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moss_Landing_Power_Plant_p1270026.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Moss_Landing_Power_Plant_p1270026.jpg/220px-Moss_Landing_Power_Plant_p1270026.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Moss_Landing_Power_Plant_p1270026.jpg/330px-Moss_Landing_Power_Plant_p1270026.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Moss_Landing_Power_Plant_p1270026.jpg/440px-Moss_Landing_Power_Plant_p1270026.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moss_Landing_Power_Plant_p1270026.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Moss_Landing_Power_Plant" title="Moss Landing Power Plant">Moss Landing Power Plant</a>, the state's largest power production source</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar_Plant_kl.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Solar_Plant_kl.jpg/220px-Solar_Plant_kl.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Solar_Plant_kl.jpg/330px-Solar_Plant_kl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Solar_Plant_kl.jpg/440px-Solar_Plant_kl.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1008" data-file-height="679" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solar_Plant_kl.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Part of the 354 MW <a href="/wiki/SEGS" class="mw-redirect" title="SEGS">SEGS</a> solar complex in northern <a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino_County,_California" title="San Bernardino County, California">San Bernardino County, California</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_use_in_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy use in California">Energy use in California</a></div>
<p>Because it is the most populous United States state, California is one of the country's largest users of energy. However because of its high energy rates, conservation mandates, mild weather in the largest population centers and strong environmental movement, its <i>per capita</i> energy use is one of the smallest of any United States state.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[175]</a></sup> Due to the high electricity demand, California imports more electricity than any other state, primarily hydroelectric power from states in the Pacific Northwest (via <a href="/wiki/Path_15" title="Path 15">Path 15</a> and <a href="/wiki/Path_66" title="Path 66">Path 66</a>) and coal- and natural gas-fired production from the desert Southwest via <a href="/wiki/Path_46" title="Path 46">Path 46</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a result of the state's strong environmental movement, California has some of the most aggressive <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> goals in the United States, with a target for California to obtain a third of its electricity from renewables by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[177]</a></sup> Currently, several <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar power plants">solar power plants</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Solar_Energy_Generating_Systems" title="Solar Energy Generating Systems">Solar Energy Generating Systems</a> facility are located in the <a href="/wiki/Mojave_Desert" title="Mojave Desert">Mojave Desert</a>. <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_California" title="Wind power in California">California's wind farms</a> include <a href="/wiki/Altamont_Pass_Wind_Farm" title="Altamont Pass Wind Farm">Altamont Pass</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Gorgonio_Pass_Wind_Farm" title="San Gorgonio Pass Wind Farm">San Gorgonio Pass</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tehachapi_Pass_Wind_Farm" title="Tehachapi Pass Wind Farm">Tehachapi Pass</a>. Several dams across the state provide <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydro-electric power</a>. It would be possible to convert the total supply to 100% renewable energy, including heating, cooling and mobility, by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state's crude oil and natural gas deposits are located in the Central Valley and along the coast, including the large <a href="/wiki/Midway-Sunset_Oil_Field" title="Midway-Sunset Oil Field">Midway-Sunset Oil Field</a>. Natural gas-fired <a href="/wiki/Power_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Power plants">power plants</a> typically account for more than one-half of state electricity generation.</p>
<p>California is also home to two major <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a> plants: <a href="/wiki/Diablo_Canyon_Power_Plant" title="Diablo Canyon Power Plant">Diablo Canyon</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Onofre_Nuclear_Generating_Station" title="San Onofre Nuclear Generating Station">San Onofre</a>, the latter having been shut down in 2013. Also voters banned the approval of new nuclear power plants since the late 1970s because of concerns over <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_waste_disposal" class="mw-redirect" title="Radioactive waste disposal">radioactive waste disposal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Doyle_2009_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doyle_2009-188">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[note 4]</a></sup> In addition, several cities such as Oakland, <a href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California" title="Berkeley, California">Berkeley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Davis,_California" title="Davis, California">Davis</a> have declared themselves as <a href="/wiki/Nuclear-free_zone" title="Nuclear-free zone">nuclear-free zones</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_California" title="Transportation in California">Transportation in California</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GoldenGateBridge-001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/GoldenGateBridge-001.jpg/220px-GoldenGateBridge-001.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/GoldenGateBridge-001.jpg/330px-GoldenGateBridge-001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/GoldenGateBridge-001.jpg/440px-GoldenGateBridge-001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GoldenGateBridge-001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Bridge" title="Golden Gate Bridge">Golden Gate Bridge</a> in San Francisco, one of California's most famous landmarks</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glendalefreeway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Glendalefreeway.jpg/220px-Glendalefreeway.jpg" width="220" height="75" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Glendalefreeway.jpg/330px-Glendalefreeway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Glendalefreeway.jpg/440px-Glendalefreeway.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="257" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glendalefreeway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Caltrans" class="mw-redirect" title="Caltrans">Caltrans</a> builds tall "stack" <a href="/wiki/Interchange_(road)" title="Interchange (road)">interchanges</a> with soaring ramps that offer impressive views</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>California's vast terrain is connected by an extensive system of <a href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highways" class="mw-redirect" title="Controlled-access highways">controlled-access highways</a> ('freeways'), <a href="/wiki/Limited-access_road" title="Limited-access road">limited-access roads</a> ('expressways'), and highways. California is known for its <a href="/wiki/Car_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Car culture">car culture</a>, giving California's cities a reputation for severe <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">traffic congestion</a>. Construction and maintenance of state roads and statewide transportation planning are primarily the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/California_Department_of_Transportation" title="California Department of Transportation">California Department of Transportation</a>, nicknamed "Caltrans". The rapidly growing population of the state is straining all of its transportation networks, and California has some of the worst roads in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[182]</a></sup> The Reason Foundation's 19th Annual Report on the Performance of State Highway Systems ranked California's highways the third-worst of any state, with Alaska second, and Rhode Island first.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[183]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state has been a pioneer in road construction. One of the state's more visible landmarks, the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Bridge" title="Golden Gate Bridge">Golden Gate Bridge</a>, was once the <a href="/wiki/List_of_longest_suspension_bridge_spans" title="List of longest suspension bridge spans">longest suspension bridge main span</a> in the world at 4,200 feet (1,300&#160;m) when it opened in 1937. With its orange paint and panoramic views of the bay, this highway bridge is a popular tourist attraction and also accommodates pedestrians and bicyclists. The <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco%E2%80%93Oakland_Bay_Bridge" title="San Francisco–Oakland Bay Bridge">San Francisco–Oakland Bay Bridge</a> (often abbreviated the "Bay Bridge"), completed in 1936, transports about 280,000 vehicles per day on two-decks. Its two sections meet at <a href="/wiki/Yerba_Buena_Island" title="Yerba Buena Island">Yerba Buena Island</a> through the world's largest diameter transportation bore tunnel, at 76 feet (23&#160;m) wide by 58 feet (18&#160;m) high.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[184]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Arroyo_Seco_Parkway" title="Arroyo Seco Parkway">Arroyo Seco Parkway</a>, connecting Los Angeles and <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena</a>, opened in 1940 as the first freeway in the Western United States.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[185]</a></sup> It was later extended south to the <a href="/wiki/Four_Level_Interchange" title="Four Level Interchange">Four Level Interchange</a> in downtown Los Angeles, regarded as the first <a href="/wiki/Stack_interchange" title="Stack interchange">stack interchange</a> ever built.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a> (LAX), <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">the 6th busiest airport in the world</a>, and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_International_Airport" title="San Francisco International Airport">San Francisco International Airport</a> (SFO), <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">the 21st busiest airport in the world</a>, are major hubs for trans-Pacific and transcontinental traffic. There are about a dozen important commercial airports and many more <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_California" title="List of airports in California">airports</a> throughout the state.</p>
<p>California also has several important <a href="/wiki/Seaport" class="mw-redirect" title="Seaport">seaports</a>. The giant seaport complex formed by the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Los_Angeles" title="Port of Los Angeles">Port of Los Angeles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_California#Shipping_and_transportation" title="Long Beach, California">Port of Long Beach</a> in Southern California is the largest in the country and responsible for handling about a fourth of all container cargo traffic in the United States. The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Oakland" title="Port of Oakland">Port of Oakland</a>, fourth largest in the nation, also handles trade entering from the Pacific Rim to the rest of the country. The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Stockton" title="Port of Stockton">Port of Stockton</a> is the easternmost port on the west coast of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[187]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/California_Highway_Patrol" title="California Highway Patrol">California Highway Patrol</a> is the largest statewide police agency in the United States in employment with over 10,000 employees. They are responsible for providing any police-sanctioned service to anyone on California's state maintained highways and on state property.</p>
<p>The California Department of Motor Vehicles is by far the largest in North America. By the end of 2009, the California DMV had 26,555,006 driver's licenses and ID cards on file.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[188]</a></sup> In 2010, there were 1.17 million new vehicle registrations in force.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[189]</a></sup></p>
<p>Intercity rail travel is provided by <a href="/wiki/Amtrak_California" title="Amtrak California">Amtrak California</a>, which manages the three busiest intercity rail lines in the United States outside the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Corridor" title="Northeast Corridor">Northeast Corridor</a>, all of which are funded by Caltrans. This service is becoming increasingly popular over flying and ridership is continuing to set records, especially on the LAX-SFO route.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[190]</a></sup> Integrated <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">subway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> networks are found in Los Angeles (<a href="/wiki/LACMTA" class="mw-redirect" title="LACMTA">Metro Rail</a>) and San Francisco (<a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Municipal_Railway" title="San Francisco Municipal Railway">MUNI Metro</a>). Light rail systems are also found in San Jose (<a href="/wiki/Santa_Clara_VTA_Light-rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Clara VTA Light-rail">VTA</a>), San Diego (<a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Trolley" title="San Diego Trolley">San Diego Trolley</a>), Sacramento (<a href="/wiki/Sacramento_Regional_Transit_District" title="Sacramento Regional Transit District">RT Light Rail</a>), and Northern San Diego County (<a href="/wiki/Sprinter_(San_Diego)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sprinter (San Diego)">Sprinter</a>). Furthermore, <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">commuter rail</a> networks serve the San Francisco Bay Area (<a href="/wiki/Altamont_Commuter_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Altamont Commuter Express">ACE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Bay Area Rapid Transit">BART</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caltrain" title="Caltrain">Caltrain</a>), Greater Los Angeles (<a href="/wiki/Metrolink_(Southern_California)" class="mw-redirect" title="Metrolink (Southern California)">Metrolink</a>), and San Diego County (<a href="/wiki/Coaster_(San_Diego)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coaster (San Diego)">Coaster</a>).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/California_High-Speed_Rail" title="California High-Speed Rail">California High-Speed Rail</a> Authority was created in 1996 by the state to implement an extensive 700 miles (1,100&#160;km) rail system. Construction was approved by the voters during the November 2008 general election, a $9.95 billion state bond will go toward its construction.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[191]</a></sup> Nearly all counties operate <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">bus</a> lines, and many cities operate their own city bus lines as well. Intercity bus travel is provided by <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">Greyhound</a> and Amtrak Thruway Coach.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_in_California" title="Water in California">Water in California</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kluft-Photo-Aerial-I205-California-Aqueduct-Img_0038.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Kluft-Photo-Aerial-I205-California-Aqueduct-Img_0038.jpg/220px-Kluft-Photo-Aerial-I205-California-Aqueduct-Img_0038.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Kluft-Photo-Aerial-I205-California-Aqueduct-Img_0038.jpg/330px-Kluft-Photo-Aerial-I205-California-Aqueduct-Img_0038.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Kluft-Photo-Aerial-I205-California-Aqueduct-Img_0038.jpg/440px-Kluft-Photo-Aerial-I205-California-Aqueduct-Img_0038.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kluft-Photo-Aerial-I205-California-Aqueduct-Img_0038.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An aerial view of the <a href="/wiki/Delta%E2%80%93Mendota_Canal" title="Delta–Mendota Canal">Delta–Mendota Canal</a> (left) and the <a href="/wiki/California_Aqueduct" title="California Aqueduct">California Aqueduct</a> (right), at the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_205_(California)" title="Interstate 205 (California)">Interstate 205</a> crossing west of <a href="/wiki/Tracy,_California" title="Tracy, California">Tracy</a>, conveying water from Northern to Southern California</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>California's interconnected water system is the world's largest, managing over 40,000,000 <a href="/wiki/Acre_foot" class="mw-redirect" title="Acre foot">acre feet</a> (49&#160;km<sup>3</sup>) of water per year, centered on six main systems of aqueducts and infrastructure projects.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[192]</a></sup> Water use and conservation in California is a politically divisive issue, as the state experiences periodic droughts and has to balance the demands of its large agricultural and urban sectors, especially in the arid southern portion of the state. The state's widespread redistribution of water also invites the frequent scorn of environmentalists.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/California_Water_Wars" title="California Water Wars">California Water Wars</a>, a conflict between Los Angeles and the Owens Valley over water rights, is one of the most well-known examples of the struggle to secure adequate water supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[193]</a></sup> Former California Governor Arnold Schwarzenegger said: "We've been in crisis for quite some time because we're now 38 million people and not anymore 18 million people like we were in the late 60s. So it developed into a battle between environmentalists and farmers and between the south and the north and between rural and urban. And everyone has been fighting for the last four decades about water."<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_California" title="Government of California">Government of California</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Capitol_Building_MG_1600_Sans_watermark.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Capitol_Building_MG_1600_Sans_watermark.jpg/220px-Capitol_Building_MG_1600_Sans_watermark.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Capitol_Building_MG_1600_Sans_watermark.jpg/330px-Capitol_Building_MG_1600_Sans_watermark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Capitol_Building_MG_1600_Sans_watermark.jpg/440px-Capitol_Building_MG_1600_Sans_watermark.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Capitol_Building_MG_1600_Sans_watermark.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/California_State_Capitol" title="California State Capitol">California State Capitol</a> building in <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The state's capital is <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento</a>.</p>
<p>California is organized into three <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">branches of government</a> – the <a href="/wiki/Executive_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive branch">executive branch</a> consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_California" title="Governor of California">Governor</a> and the other independently elected constitutional officers; the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative branch">legislative branch</a> consisting of the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Assembly" title="California State Assembly">Assembly</a> and <a href="/wiki/California_State_Senate" title="California State Senate">Senate</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Judicial branch">judicial branch</a> consisting of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_California" title="Supreme Court of California">Supreme Court of California</a> and lower courts. The state also allows <a href="/wiki/California_ballot_proposition" title="California ballot proposition">ballot propositions</a>: direct participation of the electorate by <a href="/wiki/Initiative" title="Initiative">initiative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Recall_election" title="Recall election">recall</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ratification" title="Ratification">ratification</a>. Before the passage of <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_14_(2010)" title="California Proposition 14 (2010)">California Proposition 14 (2010)</a>, California allowed each political party to choose whether to have a <a href="/wiki/Closed_primary" class="mw-redirect" title="Closed primary">closed primary</a> or a primary where only party members and <a href="/wiki/Independent_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent (politics)">independents</a> vote. After June 8, 2010 when Proposition 14 was approved, excepting only the United States President and county central committee offices,<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[195]</a></sup> all candidates in the primary elections are listed on the ballot with their preferred party affiliation, but they are not the official nominee of that party.<sup id="cite_ref-DB2_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB2-206">[196]</a></sup> At the primary election, the two candidates with the top votes will advance to the general election regardless of party affiliation.<sup id="cite_ref-DB2_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB2-206">[196]</a></sup> If at a special primary election, one candidate receives more than 50% of all the votes cast, they are elected to fill the vacancy and no special general election will be held.<sup id="cite_ref-DB2_206-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB2-206">[196]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Executive branch</dt>
</dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/California_executive_branch" title="California executive branch">California executive branch</a> consists of the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_California" title="Governor of California">Governor of California</a> and seven other elected constitutional officers: <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_California" title="Lieutenant Governor of California">Lieutenant Governor</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_Attorney_General" class="mw-redirect" title="California Attorney General">Attorney General</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_California" title="Secretary of State of California">Secretary of State</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_State_Controller" title="California State Controller">State Controller</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_State_Treasurer" title="California State Treasurer">State Treasurer</a>, <a href="/wiki/California_Insurance_Commissioner" title="California Insurance Commissioner">Insurance Commissioner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/California_State_Superintendent_of_Public_Instruction" title="California State Superintendent of Public Instruction">State Superintendent of Public Instruction</a>. They serve four-year terms and may be re-elected only once.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[197]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Legislative branch</dt>
</dl>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/California_State_Legislature" title="California State Legislature">California State Legislature</a> consists of a 40-member Senate and 80-member Assembly. Senators serve four-year terms and Assembly members two. Members of the Assembly are subject to <a href="/wiki/Term_limit" title="Term limit">term limits</a> of three terms, and members of the Senate are subject to term limits of two terms.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Judicial branch</dt>
</dl>
<p>California's legal system is explicitly based upon English <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a><sup id="cite_ref-Cal_Civil_Code_22.2_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cal_Civil_Code_22.2-208">[198]</a></sup> (as is the case with all other states except <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Louisiana law">Louisiana</a>) but carries a few features from Spanish <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Community_property" title="Community property">community property</a>. California's prison population grew from 25,000 in 1980 to over 170,000 in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_2007_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson_2007-209">[199]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_California" title="Capital punishment in California">Capital punishment</a> is a legal form of punishment and the state has the largest "<a href="/wiki/Death_Row" class="mw-redirect" title="Death Row">Death Row</a>" population in the country (though Texas is far more active in carrying out executions).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_California" title="Judiciary of California">California's judiciary system</a> is the largest in the United States (with a total of 1,600 judges, while the federal system has only about 840). At the apex is the seven Justices of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_California" title="Supreme Court of California">Supreme Court of California</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/California_Courts_of_Appeal" class="mw-redirect" title="California Courts of Appeal">California Courts of Appeal</a> serve as the primary <a href="/wiki/Appellate_court" title="Appellate court">appellate courts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/California_Superior_Courts" class="mw-redirect" title="California Superior Courts">California Superior Courts</a> serve as the primary <a href="/wiki/Trial_court" title="Trial court">trial courts</a>. Justices of the Supreme Court and Courts of Appeal are appointed by the Governor, but are subject to retention by the electorate every 12 years. The administration of the state's court system is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Council_of_California" title="Judicial Council of California">Judicial Council</a>, composed of the Chief Justice of the California Supreme Court, 14 judicial officers, four representatives from the <a href="/wiki/State_Bar_of_California" title="State Bar of California">State Bar of California</a>, and one member from each house of the state legislature.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_California" title="Local government in California">Local government in California</a></div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">Counties</span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_California" title="List of counties in California">List of counties in California</a></div>
<p>California is divided into 58 <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a>. Per Article 11, Section 1, of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_California" title="Constitution of California">Constitution of California</a>, they are the legal subdivisions of the state. The county government provides countywide services such as law enforcement, jails, elections and voter registration, vital records, property assessment and records, tax collection, public health, health care, social services, libraries, flood control, fire protection, animal control, agricultural regulations, building inspections, ambulance services, and education departments in charge of maintaining statewide standards.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[201]</a></sup> In addition, the county serves as the local government for all <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated areas</a>. Each county is governed by an elected <a href="/wiki/Board_of_supervisors" title="Board of supervisors">board of supervisors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaldassare199850_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaldassare199850-212">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="City_and_town_governments">City and town governments</span></h5>
<p>Incorporated cities and towns in California are either <a href="/wiki/Charter_city" title="Charter city">charter</a> or general-law municipalities.<sup id="cite_ref-Cal_Gov_Code_34502_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cal_Gov_Code_34502-103">[102]</a></sup> General-law municipalities owe their existence to state law and are consequently governed by it; charter municipalities are governed by their own city or town charters. Municipalities incorporated in the 19th century tend to be charter municipalities. All ten of the state's most populous cities are charter cities. Most small cities have a <a href="/wiki/Council-manager_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Council-manager government">council-manager</a> form of government, where the elected city council appoints a city manager to supervise the operations of the city. Some larger cities have a directly-elected mayor who oversees the city government. In many council-manager cities, the city council selects one of its members as a mayor, sometimes rotating through the council membership—but this type of mayoral position is primarily ceremonial.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_San_Francisco" title="Government of San Francisco">Government of San Francisco</a> is the only <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_city-county" title="Consolidated city-county">consolidated city-county</a> in California, where both the city and county governments have been merged into one unified jurisdiction. The <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Board_of_Supervisors" title="San Francisco Board of Supervisors">San Francisco Board of Supervisors</a> also acts as the city council and the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_San_Francisco" title="Mayor of San Francisco">Mayor of San Francisco</a> also serves as the county administrative officer.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="School_districts_and_special_districts">School districts and special districts</span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_school_districts_in_California" title="List of school districts in California">List of school districts in California</a></div>
<p>About 1,102 <a href="/wiki/School_district" title="School district">school districts</a>, independent of cities and counties, handle California's <a href="/wiki/Public_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Public education">public education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-census2012p25_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2012p25-213">[203]</a></sup> California school districts may be organized as elementary districts, high school districts, unified school districts combining elementary and high school grades, or community college districts.<sup id="cite_ref-census2012p25_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2012p25-213">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are about 3,400 <a href="/wiki/Special-purpose_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Special-purpose district">special districts</a> in California.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[204]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Special-purpose_district" class="mw-redirect" title="Special-purpose district">special district</a>, defined by California Government Code § 16271(d) as "any agency of the state for the local performance of governmental or proprietary functions within limited boundaries", provides a limited range of services within a defined geographic area. The geographic area of a special district can spread across multiple cities or counties, or could consist of only a portion of one. Most of California's special districts are <i>single-purpose districts</i>, and provide one service.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_representation">Federal representation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/California%27s_congressional_districts" title="California's congressional districts">California's congressional districts</a></div>
<p>The state of California sends <a href="/wiki/California%27s_congressional_districts" title="California's congressional districts">53</a> members to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[205]</a></sup> the nation's largest congressional state delegation. Consequently California also has the largest number of <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral votes</a> in national presidential elections, with 55. California's <a href="/wiki/U.S._Senator" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Senator">U.S. Senators</a> are <a href="/wiki/Dianne_Feinstein" title="Dianne Feinstein">Dianne Feinstein</a>, a native and former mayor of San Francisco, and <a href="/wiki/Kamala_Harris" title="Kamala Harris">Kamala Harris</a>, a native, former District Attorney from San Francisco and former Attorney General of California. In 1992, California became the first state to have a Senate delegation entirely composed of women.</p>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:307px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_California,_2016.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/United_States_presidential_election_in_California%2C_2016.svg/305px-United_States_presidential_election_in_California%2C_2016.svg.png" width="305" height="336" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/United_States_presidential_election_in_California%2C_2016.svg/458px-United_States_presidential_election_in_California%2C_2016.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/United_States_presidential_election_in_California%2C_2016.svg/610px-United_States_presidential_election_in_California%2C_2016.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2904" data-file-height="3201" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_States_presidential_election_in_California,_2016.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Treemap" class="mw-redirect" title="Treemap">Treemap</a> of the popular vote by county, 2016 presidential election.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>California has an idiosyncratic political culture compared to the rest of the country, and is sometimes regarded as a trendsetter.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[208]</a></sup> In socio-cultural mores and national politics, Californians are perceived as more <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">liberal</a> than other Americans, especially those who live in the inland states.</p>
<p>Among the political idiosyncrasies and trendsetting, California was the second state <a href="/wiki/California_gubernatorial_recall_election,_2003" class="mw-redirect" title="California gubernatorial recall election, 2003">to recall their state governor</a>, the second state to legalize abortion, and the only state to ban marriage for gay couples twice by voters (including <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_8" class="mw-redirect" title="California Proposition 8">Proposition 8 in 2008</a>). Voters also passed <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_71_(2004)" title="California Proposition 71 (2004)">Proposition 71 in 2004</a> to fund <a href="/wiki/Stem_cell" title="Stem cell">stem cell</a> research, and <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_14_(2010)" title="California Proposition 14 (2010)">Proposition 14 in 2010</a> to completely change the state's <a href="/wiki/Primary_election" title="Primary election">primary election</a> process. California has also experienced <a href="/wiki/California_Water_Wars" title="California Water Wars">disputes over water rights</a>; and a <a href="/wiki/Tax_revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Tax revolt">tax revolt</a>, culminating with the passage of <a href="/wiki/California_Proposition_13_(1978)" title="California Proposition 13 (1978)">Proposition 13 in 1978</a>, limiting state <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">property taxes</a>.</p>
<p>The state's trend towards the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> and away from the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a> can be seen in state elections. From 1899 to 1939, California had Republican governors. Since 1990, California has generally elected Democratic candidates to federal, state and local offices, including current Governor <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Brown" title="Jerry Brown">Jerry Brown</a>; however, the state has elected Republican Governors, though many of its Republican Governors, such as <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a>, tend to be considered moderate Republicans and more <a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrist</a> than the national party.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Edmund_G_Brown_Jr.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Governor of California Jerry Brown" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Edmund_G_Brown_Jr.jpg/170px-Edmund_G_Brown_Jr.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Edmund_G_Brown_Jr.jpg/255px-Edmund_G_Brown_Jr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Edmund_G_Brown_Jr.jpg/340px-Edmund_G_Brown_Jr.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="2400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Edmund_G_Brown_Jr.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Governor <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Brown" title="Jerry Brown">Jerry Brown</a> is one of the many <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a> currently in office in California.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Democrats also now hold a majority in both houses of the state legislature. There are 56 Democrats and 24 Republicans in the Assembly; and 26 Democrats and 12 Republicans in the Senate.</p>
<p>The trend towards the Democratic Party is most obvious in presidential elections; Republicans have not won California's <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral votes</a> since 1988.</p>
<p>In the United States House, the Democrats held a 34–19 edge in the CA delegation of the <a href="/wiki/110th_United_States_Congress" title="110th United States Congress">110th United States Congress</a> in 2007. As the result of <a href="/wiki/Gerrymandering" title="Gerrymandering">gerrymandering</a>, the districts in California were usually dominated by one or the other party, and few districts were considered competitive. In 2008, Californians passed Proposition 20 to empower a 14-member independent citizen commission to redraw districts for both local politicians and Congress. After the 2012 elections, when the new system took effect, Democrats gained 4 seats and held a 38–15 majority in the delegation.</p>
<p>In general, Democratic strength is centered in the populous <a href="/wiki/Coastal_California" title="Coastal California">coastal regions</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area" title="Los Angeles metropolitan area">Los Angeles metropolitan area</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a>. Republican strength is still greatest in eastern parts of the state. <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_California" title="Orange County, California">Orange County</a> also remains mostly Republican. One study ranked <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Berkeley California">Berkeley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oakland,_California" title="Oakland, California">Oakland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inglewood,_California" title="Inglewood, California">Inglewood</a> and San Francisco in the top 20 most liberal American cities; and <a href="/wiki/Bakersfield,_California" title="Bakersfield, California">Bakersfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange,_California" title="Orange, California">Orange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Escondido,_California" title="Escondido, California">Escondido</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garden_Grove,_California" title="Garden Grove, California">Garden Grove</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Simi_Valley,_California" title="Simi Valley, California">Simi Valley</a> in the top 20 most conservative cities.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[209]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2012, out of the 23,802,577 people eligible to vote, 18,245,970 people were registered to vote.<sup id="cite_ref-SoS2012GenVotRegStats_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SoS2012GenVotRegStats-220">[210]</a></sup> Of the people registered, the three largest registered groups were Democrats (7,966,422), Republicans (5,356,608), and <a href="/wiki/Decline_to_State" title="Decline to State">Decline to State</a> (3,820,545).<sup id="cite_ref-SoS2012GenVotRegStats_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SoS2012GenVotRegStats-220">[210]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles County">Los Angeles County</a> had the largest number of registered Democrats (2,430,612) and Republicans (1,037,031) of any county in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-SoS2012GenVotRegStats_220-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SoS2012GenVotRegStats-220">[210]</a></sup></p>

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Coast_Guard_Island_May_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Coast Guard Island in the Oakland Estuary" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Coast_Guard_Island_May_2009.jpg/150px-Coast_Guard_Island_May_2009.jpg" width="150" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Coast_Guard_Island_May_2009.jpg/225px-Coast_Guard_Island_May_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Coast_Guard_Island_May_2009.jpg/300px-Coast_Guard_Island_May_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center;background-color:transparent">United States Armed Forces in California. From left to right: <a href="/wiki/Fort_Irwin_National_Training_Center" title="Fort Irwin National Training Center">Fort Irwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Camp_Pendleton" title="Marine Corps Base Camp Pendleton">Camp Pendleton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_North_Island" title="Naval Air Station North Island">NAS North Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beale_Air_Force_Base" title="Beale Air Force Base">Beale Air Force Base</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coast_Guard_Island" title="Coast Guard Island">Coast Guard Island</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p>In California, as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">U.S. Department of Defense</a> had a total of 117,806 <a href="/wiki/Active_duty" title="Active duty">active duty</a> servicemembers of which 88,370 were <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">Sailors</a> or <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">Marines</a>, 18,339 were <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">Airmen</a>, and 11,097 were <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">Soldiers</a>, with 61,365 Department of Defense civilian employees. Additionally, there were a total of 57,792 <a href="/wiki/Reserve_components_of_the_United_States_Armed_Forces" title="Reserve components of the United States Armed Forces">Reservists and Guardsman</a> in California.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles County">Los Angeles County</a> was the largest origin of military recruits in the United States by county, with 1,437 individuals enlisting in the military.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[212]</a></sup> However, as of 2002, Californians were relatively under-represented in the military as a proportion to its population.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[213]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, California, had 2,569,340 veterans of United States <a href="/wiki/Military_service" title="Military service">military service</a>: 504,010 served in World War II, 301,034 in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a>, 754,682 during the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>, and 278,003 during 1990–2000 (including the Persian Gulf War).<sup id="cite_ref-City_Data_CA_Armed_Forces_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-City_Data_CA_Armed_Forces-224">[214]</a></sup> As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=California&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 1,942,775 veterans living in California, of which 1,457,875 served during a period of armed conflict, and just over four thousand served <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">before World War II</a> (the largest population of this group of any state).<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[215]</a></sup></p>
<p>California's military forces consist of the <a href="/wiki/California_National_Guard" title="California National Guard">Army and Air National Guard</a>, the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Military_Reserve" title="California State Military Reserve">naval and state military reserve</a> (militia), and the <a href="/wiki/California_Cadet_Corps" title="California Cadet Corps">California Cadet Corps</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<p>California has a <a href="/wiki/City_twinning" class="mw-redirect" title="City twinning">twinning arrangement</a> with <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Catalonia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Catalonia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Catalonia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Catalonia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Flag_of_Catalonia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Catalonia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[216]</a></sup></p>

Kleinhenz; Kimberly Ritter-Martinez; Rafael De Anda; Elizabeth Avila (August 2012). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://laedc.org/reports/AerospaceinSoCal_0812.pdf">"The Aerospace Industry in Southern California"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. laedc.org. p.&#160;10<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">June 25,</span> 2013</span>. <q>In 1987, California accounted for one in four aerospace jobs nationally, and in Los Angeles County, the share was one in ten. Following the collapse of the Soviet Union and the end of the Cold War, the Department of Defense (DOD) sharply curtailed procurement spending. In 1995, DOD spending fell below $50 billion for the first time since 1982. Nowhere in the country were the changes in Pentagon outlays more apparent than in Southern California.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACalifornia&amp;rft.au=Elizabeth+Avila&amp;rft.au=Kimberly+Ritter-Martinez&amp;rft.au=Rafael+De+Anda&amp;rft.au=Robert+A.+Kleinhenz&amp;rft.btitle=The+Aerospace+Industry+in+Southern+California&amp;rft.date=2012-08&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Flaedc.org%2Freports%2FAerospaceinSoCal_0812.pdf&amp;rft.pages=10&amp;rft.pub=laedc.org&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span><br />
